


[#R3AgencyIntro_General]: Restatement (Third) of Agency, Introduction (consensual relationships, three-party structure, and legal consequences of agency).

[#R3AgencyIntro_Inclusions]: Restatement (Third) of Agency, Introduction (employment relationships, respondeat superior, fiduciary duties, and relationships excluded from common-law agency definition).

[#R3AgencyIntro_Organizations]: Restatement (Third) of Agency, Introduction (application of agency doctrine to corporations, partnerships, business organizations, and governmental entities).

[#R3AgencyIntro_Statutes]: Restatement (Third) of Agency, Introduction (five types of relationships between common-law agency doctrine and statutory material).

[#R3AgencyIntro_RN]: Restatement (Third) of Agency, Introduction, Reporter's Notes (comparison with Restatement Second, Agency; historical development; and comparative law references).

[#R3Agency4_IntroNote]: Restatement (Third) of Agency, Chapter 4, Introductory Note (ratification replicates consequences of actual authority after the fact; relation-back effect; exoneration of agent; fairness considerations for third parties).

[#R3Agency401]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.01 (Ratification Defined).

[#R3Agency401cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.01 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 2.01, 4.02-4.08, and actual authority).

[#R3Agency401cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.01 cmt. b (ratification as act and set of effects; creates consequences of actual authority; relation-back to time of agent's act; agent exoneration; clarifies ambiguous authority).

[#R3Agency401cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.01 cmt. c (manifestation of assent: no communication required; knowledge of material facts; multiple coprincipals must each ratify; fairness to third parties).

[#R3Agency401cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.01 cmt. d (unilateral act: no communication necessary; effective without agent or third-party knowledge; distinction from actual authority's bilateral creation).

[#R3Agency402]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.02 (Effect of Ratification).

[#R3Agency402cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.02 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 4.01, 4.05-4.08, and related sections).

[#R3Agency402cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.02 cmt. b (relation-back effect: legal consequences determined as of time of agent's act; notification and knowledge imputed to principal; irrevocability of ratification once made).

[#R3Agency402cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.02 cmt. c (consequences as between principal and agent: eliminates breach-of-authority claims; agent's duty of obedience fulfilled retroactively; agent no longer liable to principal).

[#R3Agency402cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.02 cmt. d (consequences for third parties: principal becomes bound; third party bound as originally intended; agent's warranty-of-authority liability eliminated).

[#R3Agency402cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.02 cmt. e (limitations: ratification to avoid loss ineffective; voidable if induced by misconduct; intervening rights of third parties protected under § 4.05).

[#R3Agency403]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.03 (Acts That May Be Ratified).

[#R3Agency403cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.03 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 1.01, 4.01, 4.02, and agency relationship).

[#R3Agency403cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.03 cmt. b (purported to act requirement: actor must have purported or assumed to act on behalf of ratifier; ratification creates agency relationship retroactively; undisclosed principals may ratify).

[#R3Agency403cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.03 cmt. c (forgeries: rejection of traditional rule barring ratification; UCC § 3-403(a) permits ratification of unauthorized signatures including forgeries; principal's interest in obtaining transaction benefits).

[#R3Agency404]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.04 (Capacity to Ratify).

[#R3Agency404cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.04 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 1.04(5), 3.04, and capacity requirements).

[#R3Agency404cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.04 cmt. b (capacity to be principal: ratification requires capacity at time of ratifying; no requirement of capacity at time of original act; rejection of Restatement Second requirement; minors may ratify upon majority; personal representatives may ratify).

[#R3Agency404cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.04 cmt. c (nonexistent principals: corporations yet to be formed; adoption vs. ratification; no relation-back effect for adoption; promoter liability; statutory variations on promoter liability).

[#R3Agency405]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.05 (Timing of Ratification).

[#R3Agency405cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.05 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 4.01, 4.02, and timing limitations).

[#R3Agency405cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.05 cmt. b (temporal limits: fairness to third parties; unilateral power of ratification; limits beyond agency law doctrines).

[#R3Agency405cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.05 cmt. c (third party's withdrawal: manifestation of intention to withdraw before ratification; releases third party from uncertain period; incentive for prompt ratification; prevents speculation at third party's expense).

[#R3Agency405cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.05 cmt. d (material change in circumstances: inequitable to bind third party; third party may avoid or elect to be bound; alternate arrangements by third party).

[#R3Agency405cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.05 cmt. e (crystallized rights: ratification ineffective to deprive person of fixed right; timing deadlines for exercising rights; rights that accrue prior to ratification protected).

[#R3Agency406]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.06 (Knowledge Requisite to Ratification).

[#R3Agency406cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.06 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 1.02, 1.04(4), 4.01, 4.02, and 4.08).

[#R3Agency406cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.06 cmt. b (effect of lack of knowledge: ratification without knowledge of material facts not binding; burden on party establishing ratification; actual knowledge required, not notice; estoppel under § 4.08).

[#R3Agency406cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.06 cmt. c (material facts: relevance to principal's consent; definitions of materiality; facts affecting legal relations; knowledge requirement for multiple coprincipals).

[#R3Agency406cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.06 cmt. d (risk of lack of knowledge: principal may choose to ratify without knowing material facts; deliberate ignorance; assumption of risk; factfinder may infer choice from circumstances).

[#R3Agency406cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.06 cmt. e (source of knowledge: does not matter whether from agent or elsewhere; agent likely source but not required; ratification concerns past acts, not future events; analogous to contract avoidance for misrepresentation or mistake).

[#R3Agency407]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.07 (No Partial Ratification).

[#R3Agency407cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.07 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 4.01(2) and ratification requirements).

[#R3Agency407cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.07 cmt. b (burdens accompany benefits: principal cannot ratify favorable elements while rejecting unfavorable ones; ratification of contract includes ratification of agent's inducing representations; economic benefits and legal consequences inseparable).

[#R3Agency407cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.07 cmt. c (single transaction: multiple independent transactions not encompassed by ratification of one; distinct but interrelated components may constitute single transaction; fairness to third parties).

[#R3Agency408]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.08 (Estoppel to Deny Ratification).

[#R3Agency408cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.08 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 2.05, 2.06, 3.02, and related estoppel provisions).

[#R3Agency408cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.08 cmt. b (scope of doctrine: manifestation inducing detrimental reliance; distinction from actual ratification; ratification ordinarily satisfies requirements; estoppel operates only in favor of misled party; discretionary remedy; irrevocability of true ratification vs. estoppel).

[#R3Agency408cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 4.08 cmt. c (lack of capacity at time of original act: estoppel to deny capacity when person later has capacity; estoppel to deny formal requirements like writings; failure to correct third party's erroneous belief after learning of it).


[#R3Agency501]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.01 (Notifications and Notice—In General).

[#R3Agency501cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.01 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 1.03, 1.04(4), 5.02-5.04, and definitions of manifestation, notice, and notification).

[#R3Agency501cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.01 cmt. b (notice defined: inclusive term; person has notice through knowledge, reason to know, effective notification, should know, or imputation; distinction between reason to know and should know; rejection of constructive notice terminology).

[#R3Agency501cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.01 cmt. c (notification defined: manifestation to affect legal rights; public filings and specific communications; informative vs. performative content; intention to affect legal relations).

[#R3Agency501cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.01 cmt. d (statutory usage: UCC § 1-202 definitions; Uniform Partnership Act 1997 § 102 provisions; reasonable steps to inform).

[#R3Agency502]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.02 (Notification Given by or to an Agent).

[#R3Agency502cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.02 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 5.01, 5.03-5.04, and effectiveness of notifications).

[#R3Agency502cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.02 cmt. b (nature and effect of notification: actual or apparent authority required; effectiveness regardless of agent's transmission, understanding, or memory; no downward imputation to agent; undisclosed principal may receive effective notification; custom and industry practice; position-based authority; estoppel and ratification).

[#R3Agency502cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.02 cmt. c (agent acting adversely to principal: notification effective unless third party knows or has reason to know; lack of reason to doubt communications; duty of good faith; reasonable belief in customary routines).

[#R3Agency503]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 (Imputation of Notice of Fact to Principal).

[#R3Agency503cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 1.04(4), 5.01-5.02, 5.04, and imputation principles).

[#R3Agency503cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 cmt. b (justifications for imputation: agent links principal to external world; agent's duty to transmit material facts; principal's right to control; incentives for careful agent selection and monitoring; no rebuttal by principal's instruction not to communicate; knowledge vs. relevance to claims and defenses; fidelity bond exception; service provider assessments).

[#R3Agency503cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 cmt. c (imputation in organizational settings: notification procedures; large organizations; designated recipients; internal communications).

[#R3Agency503cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 cmt. d (effect on principal's legal relations: contract formation; tort liability; rights and defenses; property transactions; statute of limitations; regulatory compliance).

[#R3Agency503cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 cmt. e (acquiring knowledge or reason to know: observation; inquiry; communications from third parties; casual or happenstance acquisition; agent's investigation duties).

[#R3Agency503cmt_f]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 cmt. f (when notice imputed: time at which agent knows or has reason to know; material to agent's duties; relation to transaction with third party).

[#R3Agency503cmt_g]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.03 cmt. g (no downward imputation: principal's knowledge not imputed to agent; regulatory contexts may vary; principal's duty to inform agent under § 8.15).

[#R3Agency504]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.04 (An Agent Who Acts Adversely to a Principal).

[#R3Agency504cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.04 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 5.02-5.03, 8.01-8.06, and adverse action definition).

[#R3Agency504cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.04 cmt. b (adverse action defined: agent acts for own benefit or another's; breach of fiduciary duty; competitive activity; self-dealing; undisclosed conflicts of interest).

[#R3Agency504cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.04 cmt. c (fraud exception to imputation: agent's knowledge not imputed when agent defrauds principal; third party's knowledge of adverse action prevents imputation; solely for agent's benefit; principal as victim).

[#R3Agency504cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.04 cmt. d (third party's knowledge: actual knowledge or reason to know; circumstances indicating agent's adverse position; unusual transaction terms; agent's financial distress).

[#R3Agency504cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.04 cmt. e (duty not to disclose: professional confidentiality; attorney-client privilege; statutory prohibitions; competing loyalties; agent as dual agent).

[#R3Agency504cmt_f]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 5.04 cmt. f (effect on notifications: notification given or received by adverse agent ineffective when third party knows or has reason to know; protection for innocent third parties; reasonable reliance).

[#R3Agency601cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.01 cmt. c (contract made on behalf of disclosed principal: identification in contract; parol evidence admissible to identify principal but not to delete identified party; corporate agents).

[#R3Agency601cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.01 cmt. d (agent as party to contract: explicit agreement; guaranty; surety; sealed instruments; notary acknowledgments; signature formats).

[#R3Agency601cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.01 cmt. e (agent's position as party: defenses arising from transaction; personal defenses; no warranty-of-authority liability when agent is party).

[#R3Agency601cmt_f]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.01 cmt. f (sealed and negotiable instruments: legislative abolition of seal distinctions; UCC provisions; contemporary expectations).

[#R3Agency602]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.02 (Agent for Unidentified Principal).

[#R3Agency602cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.02 cmt. b (bases of contractual liability: agent becomes party unless agreed otherwise; third party cannot assess principal's creditworthiness without identity; bargain principle; promissory estoppel; comparison with disclosed and undisclosed principals).

[#R3Agency602cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.02 cmt. c (contract made on behalf of unidentified principal: source of notice irrelevant; disclosure contrary to instructions; multiple principals; misrepresentation of identity under § 6.11(4); nonexistent principals under § 6.04).

[#R3Agency602cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.02 cmt. d (notice of principal's identity and agent's status: reasonably sufficient facts; trade names insufficient; presumption against requiring public-record searches; custom in particular industries; LLC and organizational contexts; consignment relationships).

[#R3Agency603cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.03 cmt. b (rationales for contractual liability: departure from bargain principle; agent and principal as parties; third party's reasonable expectations; commercial convenience; notification effectiveness; no implicit representation that agent acts alone).

[#R3Agency603cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.03 cmt. c (contract made on behalf of undisclosed principal: actual authority required; no apparent authority; estoppel under § 2.06; ratification under § 4.03; instructions to conceal identity; agent for multiple principals).

[#R3Agency603cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.03 cmt. d (circumstances affecting rights or liabilities: contract excluding undisclosed principal; non-assignability clauses insufficient; performance by principal; principal's right to performance; material change in third party's duties; personal services; substantial interest test).

[#R3Agency603cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.03 cmt. e (agent's position as party: right to sue; subject to liability; defenses from transaction and personal defenses).

[#R3Agency606]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.06 (Setoff).

[#R3Agency606cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.06 cmt. b (disclosed principal: third party may assert setoff against principal arising from agent-principal contract if principal and agent so agreed or third party relied on principal's manifestation).

[#R3Agency606cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.06 cmt. c (unidentified or undisclosed principal: third party may assert setoff against principal for claims against agent arising before third party has notice of principal's existence or identity).

[#R3Agency607]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.07 (Settlement with Agent by Principal or Third Party).

[#R3Agency607cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.07 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 6.01-6.03, and settlement effects).

[#R3Agency607cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.07 cmt. b (principal's settlement with agent: disclosed principal not discharged unless third party agreed or agent had authority; unidentified or undisclosed principal discharged if settlement before third party has notice).

[#R3Agency607cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.07 cmt. c (third party's settlement with agent: principal discharged if agent has actual or apparent authority; disclosed principal; unidentified or undisclosed principal discharged if before principal has notice of third party's claim).

[#R3Agency608cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.08 cmt. b (dealings that affect principal's liability: disclosed principal; modifications and rescissions; agent's authority; unidentified or undisclosed principal; third party's reasonable reliance; notice requirements).

[#R3Agency608cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.08 cmt. c (dealings that affect third party's liability to principal: agent must have actual or apparent authority; third party cannot elect to perform to agent when principal disclosed or identified).

[#R3Agency609]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.09 (Effect of Judgment Against Agent or Principal).

[#R3Agency609cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.09 cmt. c (judgment on contract made on behalf of undisclosed principal: rejection of election rule; liability discharged only upon satisfaction; parties' expectations; no windfall to third party; no predictability under election rule).

[#R3Agency609cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.09 cmt. d (manifestation by third party to look only to principal or agent: substituted contract; consideration required; detrimental reliance; discharge through settlement).

[#R3Agency610cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.10 cmt. b (basis for warranty: agent's implied representation; third party's reasonable reliance; strict liability regardless of agent's knowledge; ratification eliminates liability; agent as party to contract).

[#R3Agency610cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 6.10 cmt. d (exceptions and limitations: third party's knowledge of lack of authority; third party's negligence; agent's reasonable belief; warranty disclaimers).

[#R3Agency701]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.01 (Agent's Liability to Third Party).

[#R3Agency701cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.01 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 7.02, 8.01-8.12, and agent's tortious conduct).

[#R3Agency701cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.01 cmt. b (in general: agent liable for own torts regardless of actual authority, apparent authority, or scope of employment; justification for individual responsibility; statutory immunities; encouraging responsible conduct; agent as source of recovery).

[#R3Agency701cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.01 cmt. c (constitutions, statutes, regulations, and ordinances: violation subjects agent to liability unless inconsistent with statute; explicit liability provisions; CERCLA operator liability; Title VII employer-only liability; strict liability statutes).

[#R3Agency701cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.01 cmt. d (agent's own tortious conduct: no respondeat inferior; no liability for principal's or coagent's torts; superior position alone insufficient; supervisory failures; officer participation in wrongful conduct; no veil-piercing required; requisite intention or knowledge; duty of inquiry; reliance on principal's statements).

[#R3Agency701cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.01 cmt. e (privileged conduct: privilege defined; consent-based and law-based privileges; delegation to agent; purpose requirement; reasonable belief; instructions as basis for belief; agent's advice and reporting functions; conditional privilege against defamation; immunity distinguished).

[#R3Agency702]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.02 (Duty to Principal; Duty to Third Party).

[#R3Agency702cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.02 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 8.01-8.12, and breach of duty to principal not independent basis for liability to third party).

[#R3Agency702cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.02 cmt. b (in general: breach of duty to principal may subject agent to liability to third party when agent also breaches duty to third party; sources of duty to third party include tort law, contract, third-party beneficiary status, assumption of duties, or statute).

[#R3Agency702cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.02 cmt. c (physical harm: duty to exercise reasonable care; undertaking to perform principal's duty; harm to property; specific funds as property; contractual obligations creating tort duties; limited control; gratuitous assumption of duty; increased risk or reliance).

[#R3Agency702cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 7.02 cmt. d (economic loss: no liability for pure economic loss absent duty to third party; misrepresentations subject agent to liability; fraudulent and negligent misrepresentation; organizational principals; third-party beneficiary status; promise requirement; manifestation of intention; lawful instructions without promise).

[#R3Agency805cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.05 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 8.01-8.04, 8.06, 8.12, and duties regarding property and information).

[#R3Agency805cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.05 cmt. b (use of principal's property: tangible and intangible property; unauthorized use; personal benefit; benefit to third party; return of property upon termination).

[#R3Agency805cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.05 cmt. c (confidential information: trade secrets; customer lists; business strategies; duty continues after termination; proper and improper use; principal's consent; disclosure required by law).

[#R3Agency806]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.06 (Principal's Consent).

[#R3Agency806cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.06 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 8.01-8.05, and requirements for effective consent).

[#R3Agency806cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.06 cmt. b (informed consent: material facts disclosed; agent's duty to disclose; manifestation of assent; timing of consent; consent to specific transaction vs. general categories; facts known to principal).

[#R3Agency806cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.06 cmt. c (fair dealing in obtaining consent: no overreaching; no undue influence; independent judgment; adequate consideration when required).


[#R3Agency807]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.07 (Duty Created by Contract).

[#R3Agency807cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.07 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to Restatement Second, Contracts, and contract-based duties).

[#R3Agency807cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.07 cmt. b (express and implied terms: bilateral and unilateral contracts; consideration; promissory estoppel; ongoing relationships; compensation agreements; termination provisions).

[#R3Agency807cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.07 cmt. c (promise that induces reliance: definite misrepresentation; reasonable reliance; detrimental reliance; gratuitous undertakings; estoppel principles; seasonal ticket illustration).

[#R3Agency808]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.08 (Duties of Care, Competence, and Diligence).

[#R3Agency808cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.08 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to § 1.04(3) and duties of care, competence, and diligence).

[#R3Agency808cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.08 cmt. b (common-law and statutory duties: benchmarks and measures; contract provisions; raised or lowered standards; tort-law duties; vicarious liability; indemnification obligations; statutory standards for officers and partners; regulatory violations; Regulation T illustration).

[#R3Agency808cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.08 cmt. c (duty of competence: trade or profession standards; skill and knowledge; claimed expertise; superior actual knowledge; investment management illustrations).

[#R3Agency808cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.08 cmt. d (duty of diligence: bringing competence to bear; scope limited by undertaking; special relationships; nondiscretionary vs. discretionary accounts; reasonable efforts not guaranteed results).

[#R3Agency808cmt_e]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.08 cmt. e (gratuitous agents: same standard of care; voluntary undertaking; no lesser duty; termination right).

[#R3Agency809]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.09 (Compliance with Lawful Instructions).

[#R3Agency809cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.09 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 2.01-2.02, 8.01, 8.08, and duty to comply with instructions).

[#R3Agency809cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.09 cmt. b (duty to act within scope of actual authority: reasonable interpretation; compliance with instructions; unauthorized acts subject agent to liability; changed circumstances; emergency situations; inability to communicate with principal).

[#R3Agency809cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.09 cmt. c (unlawful instructions: no duty to comply; criminal conduct; tortious conduct; agent's independent liability).

[#R3Agency810]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.10 (Duty of Good Conduct).

[#R3Agency810cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.10 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to § 8.15, and duty of good conduct).

[#R3Agency810cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.10 cmt. b (conduct reflecting on principal: agent's reputation; criminal conduct; moral turpitude; harm to principal's business reputation; association with principal; public-facing agents; termination for cause).

[#R3Agency811]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.11 (Duty to Provide Information).

[#R3Agency811cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.11 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 5.03, 8.01, 8.08, and duty to provide information).

[#R3Agency811cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.11 cmt. b (material facts: reasonable efforts; information acquired in agency capacity; source irrelevant; within scope of agency; multiple principals; confidential information conflicts; reasonable expectations; disclosure timing).

[#R3Agency811cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.11 cmt. c (what is material: significance to principal's decisions; transaction terms; third-party offers; risks; agent's own interests; duty to inquire further).

[#R3Agency811cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.11 cmt. d (relationship to agent's other duties: failure to accomplish principal's directive; expertise reliance; broker notification duties; scope of managed account).

[#R3Agency812]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.12 (Duties Regarding Principal's Property—Segregation, Record-Keeping, and Accounting).

[#R3Agency812cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.12 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to § 8.05 and managerial duties).

[#R3Agency812cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.12 cmt. b (agent's duty of care: safeguarding property; due care pending delivery; agreement may define duties).

[#R3Agency812cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.12 cmt. c (segregation of principal's property: no mingling; title in principal's name; transparent dealing; protection against agent's creditors; loss liability; agreement to contrary; custom and practice; UCC provisions).

[#R3Agency812cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.12 cmt. d (keeping and rendering accounts: fiduciary duty corollary; records maintenance; account on demand; duty without demand when appropriate; post-termination duty; agreement and reasonableness).


[#R3Agency813]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.13 (Duty Created by Contract).

[#R3Agency813cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.13 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 8.14-8.15, and contract-based duties).

[#R3Agency813cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.13 cmt. b (express and implied terms: compensation agreements; reimbursement; working conditions; termination provisions; good faith and fair dealing).

[#R3Agency814]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.14 (Duty to Indemnify).

[#R3Agency814cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.14 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 7.07-7.08, 8.08, 8.13, 8.15, and indemnification duty).

[#R3Agency814cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.14 cmt. b (payment and indemnification obligations: authorized payments; losses suffered; contract may define scope; statutory provisions; claims against agent by third parties; reasonable settlements).

[#R3Agency814cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.14 cmt. c (exceptions: agent's fault; breach of duty; illegality; agent knew or should have known of risk; unauthorized acts).

[#R3Agency815]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.15 (Principal's Duty to Deal Fairly and in Good Faith).

[#R3Agency815cmt_a]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.15 cmt. a (scope and cross-references to §§ 8.13-8.14, and duty to deal fairly).

[#R3Agency815cmt_b]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.15 cmt. b (duty to deal with agent fairly and in good faith: not fiduciary duty; does not supersede termination power; foreseeably harmful conduct; agent without fault; special characteristics creating fiduciary duties).

[#R3Agency815cmt_c]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.15 cmt. c (duty to provide information to agent: physical harm risks; pecuniary loss risks; material to professional reputation; warranty information; false information; agreement may define scope; complaint disclosure not required; Taiwan responsible person illustration).

[#R3Agency815cmt_d]: Restatement (Third) of Agency § 8.15 cmt. d (duty to refrain from conduct likely to injure agent's reputation or self-respect: reciprocal of § 8.10; association with principal; business reputation injury; reasonable self-respect; dishonest operations; stigma from association).


[#APSmith]: *A.P. Smith Mfg. Co. v. Barlow*, 13 N.J. 145, 98 A.2d 581 (1953) (validating corporate charitable donations; early articulation of corporate social responsibility within profit-seeking firms) ("*A.P. Smith*").

[#ATP]: *ATP Tour, Inc. v. Deutscher Tennis Bund*, 91 A.3d 554 (Del. 2014) (holding fee-shifting bylaws facially valid under Delaware law if adopted consistently with fiduciary duties) ("*ATP Tour*").

[#Airgas]: *Air Prods. & Chems., Inc. v. Airgas, Inc.*, 16 A.3d 48 (Del. Ch. 2011) (upholding board's right to maintain a poison pill against a hostile tender offer; reaffirming board primacy under Unocal where directors act in good faith) ("*Airgas*").

[#Aronson]: *Aronson v. Lewis*, 473 A.2d 805 (Del. 1984) (establishing the demand-futility test for derivative litigation when a board decision is challenged) ("*Aronson*").

[#Gatz]: *Auriga Cap. Corp. v. Gatz Props., LLC*, 40 A.3d 839 (Del. Ch. 2012) (LLC manager self-dealing; applying contractual analysis to LLC operating agreement provisions) (“*Gatz*”).

[#Blasius]: *Blasius Indus., Inc. v. Atlas Corp.*, 564 A.2d 651 (Del. Ch. 1988) (board action interfering with the stockholder franchise triggers a compelling-justification inquiry; vote-protection doctrine) ("*Blasius*").

[#Boilermakers]: *Boilermakers Local 154 Ret. Fund v. Chevron Corp.*, 73 A.3d 934 (Del. Ch. 2013) (upholding the facial validity of exclusive-forum bylaws adopted unilaterally by boards; contractual view of bylaws and stockholder assent framework) ("*Boilermakers*").

[#Brehm]: *Brehm v. Eisner (In re Walt Disney Co. Derivative Litig.)*, 906 A.2d 27 (Del. 2006) (clarifying gross negligence, waste, and the limits of Caremark liability in executive compensation decisions; distinguishing bad faith from negligence) ("*In re Disney*").

[#CAvAFSCME]: *CA, Inc. v. AFSCME Emps. Pension Plan*, 953 A.2d 227 (Del. 2008) (invalidating shareholder-proposed bylaws that improperly restrict board fiduciary discretion) ("*CA, Inc.*").

[#CFTCOoki]: *CFTC v. Ooki DAO*, No. 3:22-cv-05416-WHO, 2023 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 146460 (N.D. Cal. June 8, 2023) (holding that a DAO may be sued as an unincorporated association; token holders who vote may be general partners with joint and several liability) ("*Ooki DAO*").

[#CMLV]: *CML V, LLC v. Bax*, 28 A.3d 1037 (Del. 2011) (LLC member oppression; applying fiduciary duty framework where operating agreement was silent on manager duties) ("*CML V*").

[#Caremark]: *In re Caremark Int'l Inc. Derivative Litig.*, 698 A.2d 959 (Del. Ch. 1996) (establishing board oversight duties and the foundational standard for compliance monitoring claims) ("*In re Caremark*").

[#Cede]: *Cede & Co. v. Technicolor, Inc.*, 634 A.2d 345 (Del. 1993) (allocating burdens of proof in fiduciary-duty litigation and clarifying cleansing effects of stockholder ratification) ("*Cede*").

[#Coggins]: *Coggins v. New England Patriots Football Club, Inc.*, 397 Mass. 525, 492 N.E.2d 1112 (1986) (close-corporation freeze-out principles; fiduciary constraints on controlling stockholders in squeeze-out transactions under Massachusetts doctrine) ("*Coggins*").

[#Corwin]: *Corwin v. KKR Fin. Holdings LLC*, 125 A.3d 304 (Del. 2015) (fully informed, uncoerced stockholder approval of a non-controller transaction cleanses fiduciary claims and invokes business judgment review with pleading-stage dismissal consequences) ("*Corwin*").

[#Cranson]: *Cranson v. Int'l Bus. Machs. Corp.*, 234 Md. 477, 200 A.2d 33 (1964) (corporation by estoppel; protecting parties who dealt with a defectively incorporated entity as if it were a corporation) ("*Cranson*").

[#CreditLyonnais]: *Credit Lyonnais Bank Nederland, N.V. v. Pathe Commc'ns Corp.*, No. Civ. A. 12150, 1991 WL 277613 (Del. Ch. Dec. 30, 1991) (directors of an insolvent corporation owe duties to the corporate enterprise and creditors, not solely to stockholders; zone of insolvency fiduciary shift) ("*Credit Lyonnais*").

[#DFC]: *DFC Glob. Corp. v. Muirfield Value Partners, L.P.*, 172 A.3d 346 (Del. 2017) (emphasizing market efficiency and deal price in appraisal valuation; skepticism of discounted cash flow models when reliable market evidence exists) ("*DFC*").

[#DartmouthCollege]: *Trs. of Dartmouth Coll. v. Woodward*, 17 U.S. (4 Wheat.) 518 (1819) (corporate charter is a contract protected by the Contracts Clause; foundational corporate personhood and constitutional protection doctrine) ("*Dartmouth College*").

[#Dell]: *Dell, Inc. v. Magnetar Glob. Event Driven Master Fund Ltd.*, 177 A.3d 1 (Del. 2017) (reinforcing deal-price primacy in appraisal actions arising from arm's-length mergers) ("*Dell*").

[#Dodge]: *Dodge v. Ford Motor Co.*, 204 Mich. 459, 170 N.W. 668 (1919) (classic statement of shareholder primacy and limits on managerial discretion to forgo profits; corporate purpose is to benefit shareholders) ("*Dodge*").

[#EquityLinked]: *Equity-Linked Invs., L.P. v. Adams*, 705 A.2d 1040 (Del. Ch. 1997) (preferred stock rights are primarily contractual, but directors still owe fiduciary duties; contract-rights-first framing in preferred/common conflict settings) ("*Equity-Linked*").

[#EvansAbney]: *Evans v. Abney*, 396 U.S. 435 (1970) (charitable trust cy pres doctrine; when trust purpose becomes impossible or impracticable, court may terminate rather than modify if settlor intent requires) ("*Evans*").

[#Fisk]: *Fisk Ventures, LLC v. Segal*, No. 3017-CC, 2008 WL 1961156 (Del. Ch. May 7, 2008) (LLC operating agreement interpretation; enforcing contractual limits on fiduciary duties and manager removal provisions) ("*Fisk Ventures*").

[#Gimbel]: *Gimbel v. Signal Cos.*, 316 A.2d 599 (Del. Ch. 1974) (DGCL substantially-all-assets line-drawing; when an asset disposition is large enough to require stockholder approval under § 271) ("*Gimbel*").

[#Guth]: *Guth v. Loft, Inc.*, 5 A.2d 503 (Del. 1939) (foundational corporate opportunity doctrine case; fiduciary may not usurp business opportunity belonging to corporation) ("*Guth*").

[#Hariton]: *Hariton v. Arco Elecs., Inc.*, 40 Del. Ch. 326 (1963) (rejecting de facto merger doctrine; transactional form chosen by parties will be respected if authorized by statute) ("*Hariton*").

[#HerzogFoundation]: *Carl J. Herzog Found., Inc. v. Univ. of Bridgeport*, 243 Conn. 1, 699 A.2d 995 (1997) (charitable corporation merger and asset transfer; applying cy pres principles when donor intent conflicts with institutional survival) ("*Herzog Foundation*").

[#Howey]: *SEC v. W.J. Howey Co.*, 328 U.S. 293 (1946) (investment-contract test for securities regulation; foundational securities-law standard requiring investment of money in common enterprise with expectation of profits from others' efforts, often applied to digital assets) ("*Howey*").

[#JonesWolf]: *Jones v. Wolf*, 443 U.S. 595 (1979) (religious organization property disputes; neutral principles of law approach to church governance and property control) ("*Jones*").

[#KahnLynch]: *Kahn v. Lynch Commc'n Sys., Inc.*, 638 A.2d 1110 (Del. 1994) (applying entire fairness to controller squeeze-outs absent procedural protections; later modified by MFW framework) ("*Kahn* (*Lynch*)").

[#KahnMFW]: *Kahn v. M&F Worldwide Corp.*, 88 A.3d 635 (Del. 2014) (establishing the MFW framework allowing business judgment review of controller mergers with dual protections: from-the-outset conditioning on both independent special committee approval and majority-of-the-minority stockholder vote) ("*Kahn* (*MFW*)").

[#Kamin]: *Kamin v. Am. Express Co.*, 86 Misc. 2d 809, 383 N.Y.S.2d 807 (Sup. Ct. 1976) (business judgment rule; courts generally will not second-guess dividend or asset-disposition decisions absent fraud, illegality, or waste) ("*Kamin*").

[#Klang]: *Klang v. Smith's Food & Drug Ctrs., Inc.*, 702 A.2d 150 (Del. 1997) (Delaware valuation and appraisal methodology; addressing how to treat valuation evidence where market indicators and other valuation methods diverge) ("*Klang*").

[#Landreth]: *Landreth Timber Co. v. Landreth*, 471 U.S. 681 (1985) (stock-versus-asset sales under securities law; sale-of-business doctrine and when stock sale constitutes securities transaction) ("*Landreth*").

[#ManhattanEye]: *Manhattan Eye, Ear & Throat Hosp. v. Spitzer*, 186 Misc. 2d 126, 715 N.Y.S.2d 575 (Sup. Ct. 1999) (nonprofit hospital conversion; attorney general oversight of charitable asset transfers and cy pres application) ("*Manhattan Eye*").

[#ManichaeanCapital]: *Manichaean Cap., LLC v. Exela Techs., Inc.*, 251 A.3d 694 (Del. Ch. 2021) (controlling stockholder identification; analyzing when stockholder or group exercises actual control sufficient to trigger entire fairness review) ("*Manichaean Capital*").

[#Marchand]: *Marchand v. Barnhill*, 212 A.3d 805 (Del. 2019) (Caremark oversight duties; board's failure to implement any system to monitor central compliance risks states a claim for breach of duty of loyalty) ("*Marchand*").

[#MartinvPeyton]: *Martin v. Peyton*, 246 N.Y. 213, 158 N.E. 77 (1927) (partnership-by-estoppel and partnership formation; distinguishing creditor protections from partnership control) ("*Martin*").

[#McDermott]: *McDermott, Inc. v. Lewis*, 531 A.2d 206 (Del. 1987) (internal affairs doctrine; Delaware's approach to choice-of-law for governance disputes involving Delaware corporations) ("*McDermott*").

[#McRitchie]: *McRitchie v. Zuckerberg*, 315 A.3d 518 (Del. Ch. 2024) (Section 220 books-and-records inspection; proper purpose analysis for stockholder investigating board composition and governance) ("*McRitchie*").

[#Meehan]: Meehan v. Shaughnessy, 404 Mass. 419, 535 N.E.2d 1255 (1989) (holding that partners owe each other a fiduciary duty of "the utmost good faith and loyalty" that continues until actual departure from the partnership; departing partners breached their fiduciary duties by secretly planning their departure, denying their intent to leave when directly asked, and unfairly soliciting clients by obtaining consents to withdraw cases without giving remaining partners fair opportunity to compete for those clients) (*”Meehan”*).

[#Meinhard]: *Meinhard v. Salmon*, 249 N.Y. 458, 164 N.E. 545 (1928) (fiduciary loyalty in joint ventures and partnership-like relationships; co-adventurers owe duty of finest loyalty, not honesty alone) ("*Meinhard*").

[#MillStreet]: *Mill St. Church of Christ v. Hogan*, 785 S.W.2d 263 (Ky. Ct. App. 1990) (religious organization governance; church property control and hierarchical versus congregational governance structures) ("*Mill Street*").

[#Moffatt]: Moffatt v. Air Canada, 2024 BCCRT 149 (Can. B.C. Civ. Res. Trib.) (holding airline liable for chatbot's misrepresentations under apparent authority principles) ("*Moffart* ").

[#NationalBiscuit]: *Nat'l Biscuit Co. v. Stroud*, 249 N.C. 467, 106 S.E.2d 692 (1959) (partnership ordinary course authority; one partner cannot unilaterally restrict another partner's authority to bind partnership in ordinary course of business) ("*National Biscuit*").

[#OberlyKirby]: *Oberly v. Kirby*, 592 A.2d 445 (Del. 1991) (nonprofit corporate governance; charitable corporation directors owe fiduciary duties to the corporation and its charitable purposes, not to donors) ("*Oberly*").

[#Omnicare]: *Omnicare, Inc. v. NCS Healthcare, Inc.*, 818 A.2d 914 (Del. 2003) (deal-protection limits; fiduciary constraints on lockups and preclusive or coercive provisions; board's ability to contract in ways that constrain future fiduciary flexibility) ("*Omnicare*").

[#PackLiquidating]: *In re Pack Liquidating, LLC*, No. 22-10797 (CTG) (Bankr. D. Del. Mar. 22, 2024) (LLC bankruptcy and entity status; analyzing whether LLC dissolved under state law prior to bankruptcy filing) ("*In re Pack Liquidating*").

[#ParamountQVC]: *Paramount Commc'ns Inc. v. QVC Network Inc.*, 637 A.2d 34 (Del. 1993) (Revlon-mode change-of-control analysis; enhanced scrutiny of deal protections in bidding contest; board must reasonably seek best value when transaction results in change of control) ("*Paramount* (*QVC*)").

[#ParamountTime]: *Paramount Commc'ns, Inc. v. Time Inc.*, 571 A.2d 1140 (Del. 1989) (no Revlon duty where transaction does not effect change of control; board may pursue long-term strategy; defensive response analyzed within enhanced scrutiny framework) ("*Paramount* (*Time*)").

[#QuadrantVertin]: *Quadrant Structured Prods. Co. v. Vertin*, 115 A.3d 535 (Del. Ch. 2015) (LLC contractual freedom; enforcing operating agreement provisions that modified or eliminated default fiduciary duties) ("*Quadrant*").

[#Rales]: *Rales v. Blasband*, 634 A.2d 927 (Del. 1993) (providing an alternative demand-futility test when no board decision is challenged; demand is excused if reasonable doubt that directors are disinterested and independent) ("*Rales*").

[#Revlon]: *Revlon, Inc. v. MacAndrews & Forbes Holdings, Inc.*, 506 A.2d 173 (Del. 1986) (sale-of-control context: board's role shifts to reasonably seeking the best value available for stockholders; enhanced scrutiny and deal-protection skepticism) ("*Revlon*").

[#Ripple]: *SEC v. Ripple Labs, Inc.*, 682 F. Supp. 3d 308 (S.D.N.Y. 2023) (Howey analysis applied to digital-asset distributions; distinguishes among transaction types in assessing investment-contract status) ("*Ripple*").

[#RotaryInternational]: *Bd. of Dirs. of Rotary Int'l v. Rotary Club of Duarte*, 481 U.S. 537 (1987) (nonprofit expressive association rights; applying constitutional limits on state regulation of membership policies in civic organizations) ("*Rotary International*").

[#Salzberg]: *Salzberg v. Sciabacucchi*, 227 A.3d 102 (Del. 2020) (federal-forum charter provisions valid under Delaware law for Securities Act claims; forum-selection clause enforcement in corporate charters) ("*Salzberg*").

[#SamuelsLido]: *Samuels v. Lido DAO*, No. 3:23-cv-01962, 2024 WL 2446228 (N.D. Cal. Dec. 5, 2024) (DAO unincorporated association liability; applying general partnership analysis to decentralized governance token holders) ("*Lido DAO*").

[#SarcuniBZx]: *Sarcuni v. bZx DAO*, 664 F. Supp. 3d 1100 (S.D. Cal. 2023) (DAO as general partnership; tokenholders who participate in governance may face personal liability as partners) ("*bZx DAO*").

[#Schnell]: *Schnell v. Chris-Craft Indus., Inc.*, 285 A.2d 437 (Del. 1971) (holding that directors cannot move up the date of the annual meeting to handicap a dissident proxy contest, because corporate actions that are technically lawful are still invalid if used for inequitable, management-entrenching purposes) ("*Schnell*").

[#Shlensky]: *Shlensky v. Wrigley*, 95 Ill. App. 2d 173, 237 N.E.2d 776 (1968) (business judgment protection for non-economic managerial decisions; directors have discretion to pursue non-financial objectives within business context) ("*Shlensky*").

[#Sinclair]: *Sinclair Oil Corp. v. Levien*, 280 A.2d 717 (Del. 1971) (distinguishing business judgment and entire fairness in parent-subsidiary transactions; entire fairness applies when parent receives benefit to exclusion of minority) ("*Sinclair*").

[#SmithVanGorkom]: *Smith v. Van Gorkom*, 488 A.2d 858 (Del. 1985) (imposing liability for grossly uninformed board decision-making; directors must inform themselves of all material information reasonably available before making business decisions) ("*Van Gorkom*").

[#SmithersvStLukes]: *Smithers v. St. Luke's-Roosevelt Hosp. Ctr.*, 281 A.D.2d 127, 723 N.Y.S.2d 426 (App. Div. 2001) (nonprofit restricted gift enforcement; donor standing to enforce charitable restrictions against hospital's diversion of funds) ("*Smithers*").

[#SternLucyWebb]: *Stern v. Lucy Webb Hayes Nat'l Training Sch. for Deaconesses & Missionaries*, 381 F. Supp. 1003 (D.D.C. 1974) (nonprofit hospital fiduciary duties; directors must exercise reasonable care and avoid self-dealing in managing charitable assets) ("*Stern*").

[#Stone]: *Stone v. Ritter*, 911 A.2d 362 (Del. 2006) (integrating Caremark oversight duties into the duty of loyalty; oversight liability requires showing directors acted in bad faith by utterly failing to implement monitoring system) ("*Stone*").

[#Tesla]: *In re Tesla Motors, Inc. Stockholder Litig.*, 2022 WL 1237185 (Del. Ch. Apr. 27, 2022) (stockholder fiduciary-duty litigation involving high-profile conflicted transaction; illustrates disclosure, process, and standard-of-review stakes in controller-adjacent settings) ("*In re Tesla*").

[#ThompsonGreen]: *Thompson & Green Mach. Co. v. Music City Lumber Co.*, 683 S.W.2d 340 (Tenn. Ct. App. 1984) (partnership dissolution and winding up; partner's duty to complete ongoing contracts and account for partnership assets) ("*Thompson & Green*").

[#Trenwick]: *Trenwick Am. Litig. Tr. v. Ernst & Young, L.L.P.*, 906 A.2d 168 (Del. Ch. 2006) (aiding and abetting breach of fiduciary duty; third-party advisor liability for knowingly participating in director wrongdoing) ("*Trenwick*").

[#UniSuper]: *UniSuper Ltd. v. News Corp.*, 898 A.2d 344 (Del. Ch. 2006) (addressing board authority and fiduciary duties in global media governance; dual-class stock and controller obligations) ("*UniSuper*").

[#Unitrin]: *Unitrin, Inc. v. Am. Gen. Corp.*, 651 A.2d 1361 (Del. 1995) (refining Unocal proportionality analysis for defensive measures; response not preclusive if shareholders retain meaningful choice) ("*Unitrin*").

[#Unocal]: *Unocal Corp. v. Mesa Petroleum Co.*, 493 A.2d 946 (Del. 1985) (enhanced scrutiny for defensive measures; board must show reasonable grounds for threat perception and a response that is neither coercive nor preclusive and is proportionate to the threat) ("*Unocal*").

[#VGSvCastiel]: *VGS, Inc. v. Castiel*, No. 17995, 2000 Del. Ch. LEXIS 122 (Del. Ch. Aug. 31, 2000) (LLC manager fiduciary duties; breach of duty of loyalty where managers acted in secret to eliminate fellow manager's control) ("*VGS*").

[#VanLoonI]: *Van Loon v. Dep't of Treasury*, 688 F. Supp. 3d 454 (W.D. Tex. 2023) (DAO tax reporting requirements; holding Treasury Department's broker definition unconstitutionally exceeds statutory authority as applied to DeFi protocols) ("*Van Loon I*").

[#VanLoonII]: *Van Loon v. United States Dep't of the Treasury*, 122 F.4th 549 (5th Cir. 2024) (Fifth Circuit reversal of district court; upholding Treasury's authority to impose tax reporting obligations on certain DeFi participants) ("*Van Loon II*").

[#VanLoonIII]: *Van Loon v. Dep't of Treasury*, No. 1:23-CV-312-RP, 2025 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 80108 (W.D. Tex. Apr. 28, 2025) (remand proceedings following Fifth Circuit; analyzing scope of broker definition as applied to specific DAO governance structures) ("*Van Loon III*").

[#VantagePoint]: *VantagePoint Venture Partners 1996 v. Examen, Inc.*, 871 A.2d 1108 (Del. 2005) (internal affairs doctrine blocks California pseudo-foreign-corporation law from overriding Delaware voting and governance rules) ("*VantagePoint*").

[#Verition]: *Verition Partners Master Fund Ltd. v. Aruba Networks, Inc.*, 210 A.3d 128 (Del. 2019) (limiting appraisal value to deal price absent reliable contrary evidence; skepticism of deal-price-less-synergies when reliable market indicators exist) ("*Verition*").

[#Walkovszky]: *Walkovszky v. Carlton*, 18 N.Y.2d 414, 223 N.E.2d 6 (1966) (veil-piercing limits; undercapitalization alone insufficient to pierce corporate veil absent showing of fraud or illegitimate purpose) ("*Walkovszky*").

[#WallaceWood]: *Wallace ex rel. Cencom Cable Income Partners II, Inc., L.P. v. Wood*, 752 A.2d 1175 (Del. Ch. 1999) (limited partnership fiduciary duties; general partner's duty when partnership agreement permits but does not mandate certain transactions) ("*Wallace*").

[#Weinberger]: *Weinberger v. UOP, Inc.*, 457 A.2d 701 (Del. 1983) (controller cash-out mergers subject to entire fairness review requiring fair dealing and fair price; modernized appraisal valuation methodology beyond rigid Delaware block method) ("*Weinberger*").

[#WestPalmBeach]: *W. Palm Beach Firefighters' Pension Fund v. Moelis & Co.*, 311 A.3d 809 (Del. Ch. 2024) (dual-class stock recapitalization; analyzing whether controlling stockholder transaction requires majority-of-the-minority vote) ("*West Palm Beach*").

[#Wilkes]: *Wilkes v. Springside Nursing Home, Inc.*, 370 Mass. 842, 353 N.E.2d 657 (1976) (close corporation minority oppression; balancing test for majority action requiring legitimate business purpose and consideration of less harmful alternatives) ("*Wilkes*").

[#Zahn]: *Zahn v. Transamerica Corp.*, 162 F.2d 36 (3d Cir. 1947) (early minority shareholder protection and fiduciary duty case; controller's duty of fair dealing in redemption of preferred stock) ("*Zahn*").

[#Zapata]: *Zapata Corp. v. Maldonado*, 430 A.2d 779 (Del. 1981) (establishing judicial review of special litigation committee dismissals of derivative suits; two-step inquiry into committee independence and court's own business judgment) ("*Zapata*").

[#Zuckerberg]: *United Food & Com. Workers Union v. Zuckerberg*, 262 A.3d 1034 (Del. 2021) (adopting universal pre-suit demand requirement for derivative suits; demand excused only if futile under Aronson or Rales) ("*Zuckerberg*").

[#Bane]: *Bane v. Ferguson*, 890 F.2d 11 (7th Cir. 1989) (partnership expulsion requires good faith and bona fide business purpose; expelled partner entitled to fair value of partnership interest) ("*Bane*").

[#Benihana]: *Benihana of Tokyo, Inc. v. Benihana, Inc.*, 2005 WL 2922959 (Del. Ch. 2004) (director interest in transaction doesn't mandate entire fairness if disinterested directors approve after full disclosure or if transaction proven fair; DGCL § 144 safe harbor mechanics) ("*Benihana*").

[#Broz]: *Broz v. Cellular Info. Sys., Inc.*, 673 A.2d 148 (Del. 1996) (director may pursue corporate opportunity if: (1) not learned in corporate capacity, (2) not in corporation's line of business, or (3) corporation lacks financial ability or interest to pursue; modern test more protective of directors than Guth) ("*Broz*").

[#Donahue]: *Donahue v. Rodd Electrotype Co.*, 367 Mass. 578, 327 N.E.2d 505 (1975) (stockholders in close corporations owe one another substantially the same fiduciary duty of utmost good faith and loyalty as partners; controlling stockholders cannot freeze out minority through discriminatory stock redemptions) ("*Donahue*").

[#EnergyResources]: *Energy Res. Corp. v. Porter*, 14 Mass. App. Ct. 296, 438 N.E.2d 391 (1982) (officer must fully and unambiguously disclose refusal-to-deal before claiming corporate opportunity is unavailable; silence by fiduciary is equivalent to stranger's lie; Massachusetts approach more protective than Delaware's Broz) ("*Energy Resources*").

[#Kovacik]: *Kovacik v. Reed*, 49 Cal. 2d 166, 315 P.2d 314 (1961) (where one partner contributes capital and other contributes only services with no agreement on loss sharing, service partner not liable for share of capital losses; each party loses own contribution) ("*Kovacik*").

[#Nixon]: *Nixon v. Blackwell*, 626 A.2d 1366 (Del. 1993) (Delaware rejects judicially-created oppression remedy for close corporations; minority stockholders must rely on contractual protections and statutory appraisal rights, not expanded fiduciary duties; contrasts with Massachusetts Donahue doctrine) ("*Nixon*").

[#SeaLand]: *Sea-Land Servs., Inc. v. Pepper Source*, 941 F.2d 519 (7th Cir. 1991) (piercing corporate veil requires both: (1) unity of interest and ownership such that separate personalities no longer exist, and (2) circumstances showing adherence to fiction of separate existence would sanction fraud or promote injustice; addresses reverse piercing) ("*Sea-Land*").

[#Seinfeld]: *Seinfeld v. Verizon Commc'ns, Inc.*, 2006 WL 181139 (Del. Ch. Jan. 19, 2005) (stockholder seeking Section 220 books-and-records inspection must demonstrate proper purpose; credible basis to infer possible mismanagement required, not mere suspicion, curiosity, or desire for fishing expedition) ("*Seinfeld*").

[#Stroud]: *Stroud v. Grace*, 606 A.2d 75 (Del. 1992) (board adoption of bylaws or board action that has primary purpose of interfering with stockholder voting franchise must be justified by compelling reasons; extends Blasius; fully informed stockholder vote ratifies board action absent fraud or illegality) ("*Stroud*").



[#Haynes]: *Haynes v. Wilder Corp. of Del.*, 721 F. Supp. 2d 1218 (M.D. Fla. 2010) (holding that a residents’ association organizing social activities was not an agent of the park owner where there was no mutual assent or right of control, despite mutual benefit and some coordination; applies Restatement (Third) of Agency § 1.01 control/consent framework).

[#Cargill]: *A. Gay Jenson Farms Co. v. Cargill, Inc.*, 309 N.W.2d 285 (Minn. 1981) (creditor became a principal for its debtor grain elevator’s contracts by exercising de facto control over operations, going beyond ordinary lender protections; classic illustration of Restatement (Second) of Agency § 14O “creditor becomes principal” doctrine).

[#Berg]: *Berg v. Nat’l Asset Mgmt. Agency*, 2012 WL 13018419 (N.D. Ga. Sept. 28, 2012) (rejecting agency and alter‑ego liability for a distressed‑asset creditor despite heavy financial oversight where there was no allegation the creditor authorized or ratified the specific employment contract or controlled its performance; distinguishes *Cargill* and limits creditor-as-principal theories).

[#Arnson]: *Arnson v. Gen. Motors Corp.*, 377 F. Supp. 209 (N.D. Ohio 1974) (holding that a franchised Chevrolet dealer was an independent merchant, not GM’s agent, absent GM control over day‑to‑day sales and customer interactions; branding and franchise agreements alone did not create agency).

[#NMMIAlumni]: *N.M. Military Inst. v. NMMI Alumni Ass’n, Inc.*, 458 P.3d 434 (N.M. 2018) (finding an agency relationship where an alumni association raised and managed funds on the school’s behalf and under its ultimate control, while emphasizing that the principal can revoke an agent’s authority and that remedies for termination sound in contract rather than forced continuation of the agency).

[#Krivo]: *Krivo Indus. Supply Co. v. Nat’l Distillers & Chem. Corp.*, 483 F.2d 1098 (5th Cir. 1973) (articulating a stringent “instrumentality” / alter‑ego standard under which a dominant creditor is liable for a debtor corporation’s obligations only when it exercises such total, participatory control that the debtor has no separate corporate will or purpose).


[#Bushey]: *Ira S. Bushey & Sons, Inc. v. United States*, 398 F.2d 167 (2d Cir. 1968) (respondeat superior; employer liable where employee’s conduct creates a foreseeable risk incident to the enterprise; “drunken sailor” drydock valve case) ("*Bushey*").

[#Butler]: *Butler v. McDonald's Sys., Inc.*, 110 F. Supp. 2d 62 (D.R.I. 2000) (franchise agency; apparent authority and right-to-control test applied to franchisor liability for franchisee's negligence) ("*Butler*").

[#Fenwick]: *Fenwick v. Unemployment Comp. Comm'n*, 133 N.J.L. 295, 44 A.2d 172 (1945) (partnership formation; co-ownership of business required; profit sharing alone insufficient to create partnership absent control and loss sharing) ("*Fenwick*").

[#GeneralAuto]: *Gen. Auto. Mfg. Co. v. Singer*, 19 Wis. 2d 528, 120 N.W.2d 659 (1963) (agent's duty of loyalty; employee cannot compete with employer or usurp business opportunities during employment) ("*General Automotive*").

[#Hoover]: *Hoover v. Sun Oil Co.*, 212 A.2d 214, 58 Del. 553 (Del. Super. Ct. 1965) (franchise agency; independent contractor status upheld where franchisor controlled results but not day-to-day details of station operation) ("*Sun Oil*").

[#HumbleOil]: *Humble Oil & Ref. Co. v. Martin*, 148 Tex. 175, 222 S.W.2d 995 (1949) (franchise agency; franchisor liable for torts at station where master agreement gave franchisor strict control over daily operations) ("*Humble Oil*").

[#Reading]: *Reading v. Attorney-General*, [1951] A.C. 507 (H.L.), *aff'g* [1948] 2 K.B. 268 (fiduciary/account of profits; soldier must disgorge profits obtained by misuse of position/uniform; agent cannot retain unauthorized profits earned by virtue of employment) ("*Reading*").

[#Vohland]: *Vohland v. Sweet*, 433 N.E.2d 860 (Ind. Ct. App. 1982) (partnership formation; profit-sharing arrangement and surrounding facts supported finding of partnership despite lack of explicit intent label) ("*Vohland*").


[#Auerbach]: *Auerbach v. Bennett*, 47 N.Y.2d 619, 393 N.E.2d 994 (1979) (special litigation committees; New York approach limits judicial review to committee's independence and procedures, unlike Delaware's Zapata standard) ("*Auerbach*").

[#Barnes]: *Barnes v. Andrews*, 298 F. 614 (S.D.N.Y. 1924) (director duty of care; causation requirement; plaintiff must show director's inattention actually caused the corporate loss) ("*Barnes*").

[#Bayer]: *Bayer v. Beran*, 49 N.Y.S.2d 2 (Sup. Ct. 1944) (duty of loyalty/entire fairness; radio advertising program featuring CEO's wife upheld as serving legitimate business purpose; early "entire fairness" application) ("*Bayer*").

[#Cheff]: *Cheff v. Mathes*, 199 A.2d 548 (Del. 1964) (defensive measures; board may repurchase stock to remove threat to corporate policy; precursor to Unocal standard) ("*Cheff*").

[#EssexUniversal]: *Essex Universal Corp. v. Yates*, 305 F.2d 572 (2d Cir. 1962) (transfer of control via stock sale + resignations; contract not illegal absent wrongful means) ("*Essex Universal*").

[#Francis]: *Francis v. United Jersey Bank*, 87 N.J. 15, 432 A.2d 814 (1981) (director duty of care; "sleeping director" liability; director cannot avoid liability for looting by other directors by remaining ignorant of financial statements) ("*Francis*").

[#Gantler]: *Gantler v. Stephens*, 965 A.2d 695 (Del. 2009) (officer fiduciary duties; explicitly holding that corporate officers owe same fiduciary duties of loyalty and care as directors) ("*Gantler*").

[#Grimes]: *Grimes v. Donald*, 673 A.2d 1207 (Del. 1996) (abdication of duty; employment agreements with severance do not inherently abdicate board duty; demand excusal distinction between abdication and due care) ("*Grimes*").

[#LeeJenkins]: *Lee v. Jenkins Bros.*, 268 F.2d 357 (2d Cir. 1959) (officer authority; president has apparent authority to bind corporation to ordinary course contracts, but not extraordinary ones like lifetime employment) ("*Lee*").

[#Lyondell]: *Lyondell Chem. Co. v. Ryan*, 970 A.2d 235 (Del. 2009) (Revlon duties; bad faith requires conscious disregard of duty; "Revlon" is not a rigid checklist of steps but a general reasonableness standard) ("*Lyondell*").

[#Ringling]: *Ringling Bros.-Barnum & Bailey Combined Shows v. Ringling*, 53 A.2d 441 (Del. 1947) (vote pooling agreements; contract between shareholders to vote together is valid; remedy for breach is invalidation of non-conforming votes) ("*Ringling*").

[#Trados]: *In re Trados Inc. S'holder Litig.*, 73 A.3d 17 (Del. Ch. 2013) (common vs. preferred; board owes duty to common stockholders when interests conflict with preferred; VC-backed exit analyzed under entire fairness) ("*In re Trados*").


[#ClarkDodge]: *Clark v. Dodge*, 269 N.Y. 410, 199 N.E. 641 (1936) (shareholder agreements; agreement to keep plaintiff as director/officer valid in close corporation where no harm to creditors or minority) ("*Clark*").

[#Elf]: *Elf Atochem N. Am., Inc. v. Jaffari*, 727 A.2d 286 (Del. 1999) (LLC contractual freedom; operating agreement's arbitration and forum selection clauses enforced; LLC is primarily a creature of contract) ("*Elf Atochem*").

[#Galler]: *Galler v. Galler*, 32 Ill. 2d 16, 203 N.E.2d 577 (1964) (close corporation shareholder agreements; upholding deviations from statutory norms in close corporations to protect reasonable expectations of owners) ("*Galler*").

[#Jordan]: *Jordan v. Duff & Phelps, Inc.*, 815 F.2d 429 (7th Cir. 1987) (close corporation fiduciary duty; duty to disclose merger discussions to employee-shareholder quitting and selling back stock) ("*Jordan*").

[#KempBeatley]: *Matter of Kemp & Beatley, Inc.*, 64 N.Y.2d 63, 473 N.E.2d 1173 (1984) (oppression/dissolution; defining oppression as frustration of reasonable expectations of the investor that were central to the decision to join) ("*Kemp*").

[#McQuade]: *McQuade v. Stoneham*, 263 N.Y. 323, 189 N.E. 234 (1934) (shareholder agreements; agreement restricting board's discretion to appoint officers/set salaries held void; traditional view contrasting with Clark v. Dodge) ("*McQuade*").

[#SmithAtlantic]: *Smith v. Atl. Props., Inc.*, 12 Mass. App. Ct. 201, 422 N.E.2d 798 (1981) (minority oppression; minority shareholder with veto power owes fiduciary duty to majority not to exercise veto recklessly to harm corporation) ("*Smith*").


[#Basic]: *Basic Inc. v. Levinson*, 485 U.S. 224 (1988) (materiality and fraud-on-the-market; rejecting bright-line "agreement-in-principle" rule for merger materiality in favor of fact-specific inquiry; rebuttable presumption of reliance in efficient markets) ("*Basic*").

[#BlueChip]: *Blue Chip Stamps v. Manor Drug Stores*, 421 U.S. 723 (1975) (Rule 10b-5 standing; limiting private right of action to actual purchasers or sellers of securities; the "Birnbaum" rule) ("*Blue Chip*").

[#Chestman]: *United States v. Chestman*, 947 F.2d 551 (2d Cir. 1991) (insider trading and family duties; mere familial relationship does not create fiduciary duty of confidentiality absent functional equivalent of dependency or control) ("*Chestman*").

[#Chiarella]: *Chiarella v. United States*, 445 U.S. 222 (1980) (classic insider trading; duty to disclose or abstain arises from specific relationship of trust and confidence, not mere possession of non-public info) ("*Chiarella*").

[#Dirks]: *Dirks v. SEC*, 463 U.S. 646 (1983) (tipper/tippee liability; tippee liable only if insider breached duty for personal benefit and tippee knew/should have known of breach) ("*Dirks*").

[#OHagan]: *United States v. O'Hagan*, 521 U.S. 642 (1997) (misappropriation theory; insider trading liability attaches when person misappropriates confidential info for securities trading in breach of duty owed to the source) ("*O'Hagan*").

[#Salman]: *Salman v. United States*, 580 U.S. 39 (2016) (insider trading; gifting confidential information to a trading relative constitutes sufficient "personal benefit" under Dirks) ("*Salman*").

[#SantaFe]: *Santa Fe Indus., Inc. v. Green*, 430 U.S. 462 (1977) (Section 10(b) limits; breach of fiduciary duty alone, without manipulation or deception, does not violate Rule 10b-5) ("*Santa Fe*").

[#TSC]: *TSC Indus., Inc. v. Northway, Inc.*, 426 U.S. 438 (1976) (materiality standard; fact is material if substantial likelihood reasonable investor would consider it important in voting/investment decision) ("*TSC*").


[#Lewis]: *Lewis v. Vogelstein*, 699 A.2d 327 (Del. Ch. 1997) (shareholder ratification and waste; informed shareholder vote cleanses duty of care/loyalty claims but cannot ratify waste) ("*Lewis*").

[#Perlman]: *Perlman v. Feldmann*, 219 F.2d 173 (2d Cir. 1955) (sale of control premium; controlling shareholder fiduciary duty when selling control block if it misappropriates a corporate asset) ("*Perlman*").

[#Salomon]: *Salomon v. A. Salomon & Co Ltd*, [1897] AC 22 (HL) (foundational entity theory; establishing the separate legal personality of the corporation distinct from its shareholders) ("*Salomon*").

[#SantaClara]: *Santa Clara Cnty. v. S. Pac. R.R. Co.*, 118 U.S. 394 (1886) (corporate personhood; extending Fourteenth Amendment equal protection rights to corporations via headnote precedent) ("*Santa Clara*").

[#TGS]: *SEC v. Tex. Gulf Sulphur Co.*, 401 F.2d 833 (2d Cir. 1968) (insider trading genesis; establishing the "disclose or abstain" rule for anyone possessing material non-public information) ("*TGS*").




[#DGCL101]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 101](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#101) (Incorporators; how corporation formed; purposes).

[#DGCL101a]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 101(a)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#101) (Who may incorporate; filing with Division of Corporations).

[#DGCL101b]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 101(b)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#101) (Lawful business or purposes).

[#DGCL101c]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 101(c)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#101) (Public utilities; applicability of Title 26).

[#DGCL102]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Contents of certificate of incorporation).

[#DGCL102a]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(a)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Required contents).

[#DGCL102a1]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(a)(1)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Corporate name; required words and distinguishability).

[#DGCL102a2]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(a)(2)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Registered office and registered agent).

[#DGCL102a3]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(a)(3)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Nature of business or purposes).

[#DGCL102a4]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(a)(4)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Authorized shares; stock classes and series; nonstock corporations).

[#DGCL102a5]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(a)(5)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Name and address of incorporator(s)).

[#DGCL102a6]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(a)(6)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Initial directors if incorporator powers terminate upon filing).

[#DGCL102b]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Optional provisions).

[#DGCL102b1]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(1)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Management provisions; powers of corporation, directors, and stockholders).

[#DGCL102b2]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(2)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Compromise and arrangement provisions).

[#DGCL102b3]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(3)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Preemptive rights).

[#DGCL102b4]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(4)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Supermajority voting requirements).

[#DGCL102b5]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(5)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Limited duration of existence).

[#DGCL102b6]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(6)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Stockholder personal liability for corporate debts).

[#DGCL102b7]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(7)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Exculpation of directors and officers for breach of fiduciary duty).

[#DGCL102b7i]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(7)(i)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Exception: breach of duty of loyalty).

[#DGCL102b7ii]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(7)(ii)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Exception: acts not in good faith or involving intentional misconduct or knowing violation of law).

[#DGCL102b7iii]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(7)(iii)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Exception: director liability under § 174).

[#DGCL102b7iv]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(7)(iv)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Exception: improper personal benefit).

[#DGCL102b7v]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(b)(7)(v)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Exception: officer liability in actions by or in the right of corporation).

[#DGCL102c]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(c)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Powers need not be recited).

[#DGCL102d]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(d)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Provisions dependent on external facts).

[#DGCL102e]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(e)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Name reservation).

[#DGCL102f]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 102(f)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#102) (Prohibition on fee-shifting provisions).

[#DGCL103]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Execution, acknowledgment, filing, and effective date).

[#DGCL103a]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(a)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Who must execute instruments).

[#DGCL103a1]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(a)(1)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Certificate of incorporation and pre-election instruments signed by incorporators).

[#DGCL103a2]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(a)(2)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Other instruments signed by authorized officers, directors, or stockholders).

[#DGCL103b]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(b)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Acknowledgment requirements).

[#DGCL103c4]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(c)(4)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Delayed effective date; suspension procedures).

[#DGCL103d]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(d)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Future effective date or time).

[#DGCL103f]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(f)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Certificate of correction).

[#DGCL103i]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 103(i)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#103) (Affidavit of extraordinary condition).

[#DGCL104]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 104](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#104) (Certificate of incorporation defined).

[#DGCL105]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 105](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#105) (Certificates as evidence).

[#DGCL106]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 106](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#106) (Commencement of corporate existence).

[#DGCL107]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 107](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#107) (Powers of incorporators).

[#DGCL108]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 108](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#108) (Organization meeting).

[#DGCL108a]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 108(a)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#108) (Purposes of organization meeting).

[#DGCL108b]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 108(b)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#108) (Notice requirements).

[#DGCL108c]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 108(c)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#108) (Action by written consent).

[#DGCL108d]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 108(d)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#108) (Action by substitute when incorporator unavailable).

[#DGCL109]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 109](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#109) (Bylaws).

[#DGCL109a]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 109(a)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#109) (Adoption, amendment, and repeal of bylaws).

[#DGCL109b]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 109(b)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#109) (Permissible bylaw provisions; prohibition on fee-shifting).

[#DGCL110]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 110](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#110) (Emergency bylaws).

[#DGCL111]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 111](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#111) (Jurisdiction to interpret corporate instruments).

[#DGCL113]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 113](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#113) (Proxy expense reimbursement).

[#DGCL114]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 114](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#114) (Application to nonstock corporations).

[#DGCL115]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 115](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#115) (Forum selection provisions).

[#DGCL116]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 116](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc01/index.html#116) (Document form, signature and delivery).


[#DGCL121]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 121](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc02/index.html#121) (General powers).

[#DGCL121a]: *Del. Code Ann.* tit. 8, [§ 121(a)](https://delcode.delaware.gov/title8/c001/sc02/index.html#121) (Powers enumerated in § 122 and all incidental powers).

[#MBCA101]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.01 (short title of state business corporation act).

[#MBCA102]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.02 (legislature retains power to amend or repeal all provisions; corporations have no vested rights in statutory terms).


[#MBCA120]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20 (general requirements for documents delivered to secretary of state for filing).

[#MBCA120a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(a) (document must satisfy this section and other applicable Act sections to be entitled to filing).

[#MBCA120b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(b) (Act must require or permit filing of document with secretary of state).

[#MBCA120c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(c) (document must contain information required by Act and may contain other information).

[#MBCA120d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(d) (document must be typewritten, printed, or if electronic in format retrievable in typewritten or printed form).

[#MBCA120e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(e) (document must be in English; corporate name need not be English if written in English letters or Arabic or Roman numerals).

[#MBCA120f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(f) (document must be signed by specified persons depending on corporate status).

[#MBCA120f1]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(f)(1) (document signed by chairman of board, president, or another officer).

[#MBCA120f2]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(f)(2) (if directors not selected or corporation not formed, document signed by incorporator).

[#MBCA120f3]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(f)(3) (if corporation in hands of receiver, trustee, or other court-appointed fiduciary, document signed by that fiduciary).

[#MBCA120g]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(g) (person signing must state name and capacity; seal, attestation, acknowledgment, and verification not required).

[#MBCA120h]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(h) (if secretary of state prescribed mandatory form under section 1.21(a), document must be in or on that form).

[#MBCA120i]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(i) (document must be delivered to secretary of state for filing; electronic delivery permitted if secretary authorizes).

[#MBCA120j]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(j) (correct filing fee and any franchise tax, license fee, or penalty must be paid when document delivered).

[#MBCA120k]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(k) (permits plan or filed document terms to depend on objectively ascertainable extrinsic facts outside document).

[#MBCA120k1]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(k)(1) (plan or filed document must state manner in which extrinsic facts will operate upon terms).

[#MBCA120k2]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(k)(2) (extrinsic facts may include market data, third-party determinations, and agreement terms).

[#MBCA120k2i]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(k)(2)(i) (extrinsic facts may include statistical or market indices, prices, rates, or economic data in nationally recognized medium).

[#MBCA120k2ii]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(k)(2)(ii) (extrinsic facts may include determination or action by any person or body, including corporation or other party).

[#MBCA120k2iii]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(k)(2)(iii) (extrinsic facts may include terms of or actions under agreements to which corporation is party).

[#MBCA120k3]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 1.20(k)(3) (definitions of filed document and plan for purposes of extrinsic facts provisions).
