[#MBCA630b5]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.30(b)(5) (holders of voting but non‑preferred shares have no preemptive rights with respect to shares having preferential distribution rights unless the preferred shares are convertible into, or carry rights to acquire, non‑preferred shares).

[#MBCA630b6]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.30(b)(6) (shares subject to preemptive rights but not purchased may, for one year, be issued to others at a price not lower than the preemptive‑offer price; later or cheaper issuances re‑trigger preemptive rights).

[#MBCA630c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.30(c) (for § 6.30, “shares” includes securities convertible into or carrying a right to subscribe for or acquire shares).

[#MBCA630cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.30 Official Comment (establishes preemptive rights as a voluntary, article‑based choice; the model language supplies detailed default rules, including exceptions for compensation and early financing rounds, and addresses multi‑class capital structures).

[#MBCA631]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.31 (authorizes a corporation to acquire its own shares and describes the effect on authorized‑share status).

[#MBCA631a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.31(a) (a corporation may acquire its own shares; acquired shares become authorized but unissued).

[#MBCA631b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.31(b) (if the articles prohibit reissue of acquired shares, they are cancelled and the number of authorized shares is reduced accordingly).

[#MBCA631cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.31 Official Comment (corporate share repurchases convert outstanding shares to authorized but unissued unless reissue is barred; boards should conform the articles to automatic reductions in authorized shares via amendments under § 10.05(f) and (g)).

[#MBCA640]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40 (sets the legal standards and measurement rules for distributions, including dividends, redemptions, and share repurchases).

[#MBCA640a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(a) (the board may authorize, and the corporation may make, distributions to shareholders, subject to article‑level restrictions and the limitations in subsection (c)).

[#MBCA640b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(b) (the board may set a non‑retroactive record date for entitlement to a distribution; if none is set for a non‑acquisition distribution, the authorization date is the record date).

[#MBCA640c1]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(c)(1) (equity‑insolvency test: no distribution if, after it is made, the corporation would be unable to pay its debts as they become due in the usual course of business).

[#MBCA640c2]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(c)(2) (balance‑sheet test: no distribution if, after it is made, total assets would be less than total liabilities plus, absent contrary articles, the amount needed to satisfy superior dissolution preferences as if the corporation were then dissolved).

[#MBCA640d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(d) (the board may base compliance with subsection (c) on reasonable financial statements, fair valuation, or any other reasonable method).

[#MBCA640e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(e) (timing rule for share acquisitions: for purchases, redemptions, and similar transactions, compliance is measured at the earlier of (i) the transfer of assets or (ii) the incurrence of indebtedness for the acquisition).

[#MBCA640f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(f) (a distribution “by indebtedness” is treated as having occurred when the debt is distributed, not when later payments are made).

[#MBCA640g]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(g) (if indebtedness is made junior to general creditors and payable only when a distribution would be lawful, it is excluded as a liability in applying the § 6.40(c) tests except as to stated principal or interest then due).

[#MBCA640h]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(h) (for corporate dissolution, liquidation, or winding up, distribution constraints are governed by chapter 14, not § 6.40).

[#MBCA640i]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40(i) (for § 6.40, “distribution” includes transfers of money or property, or incurring indebtedness, for shareholders’ benefit with respect to their shares, including dividends, redemptions, repurchases, and certain guarantees, but excludes share dividends under § 6.23).

[#MBCA640cmt1]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40 Official Comment (replaces par‑value and surplus concepts with dual solvency tests; allows flexible valuation methods; and coordinates record‑date rules with other provisions on distributions and share dividends).

[#MBCA640cmt2]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 6.40 Official Comment (explains treatment of preferential dissolution rights as deemed liabilities for the balance‑sheet test only, interaction with repurchase indebtedness (including buy‑sell arrangements), and the special treatment of deeply subordinated “distribution‑type” debt under subsection (g)).



[#MBCA701]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.01 (requires an annual shareholders’ meeting to elect directors unless they are elected by written consent; allows meetings at any place or solely by remote means; failure to hold an annual meeting does not invalidate corporate action).

[#MBCA701cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.01 Official Comment (annual‑meeting requirement secures shareholders’ rights to demand and, if necessary, obtain a court‑ordered meeting; closely held corporations often operate without regular meetings, using written consents and director holdover rules).

[#MBCA702]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.02 (governs calling, demanding, and limiting the business of special meetings).

[#MBCA702a1]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.02(a)(1) (special meetings may be called by the board or by persons authorized in the articles or bylaws).

[#MBCA702a2]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.02(a)(2) (shareholders holding at least 10 percent of votes entitled to be cast on a proposed issue may demand a special meeting, subject to an article‑level range between a lower percentage and 25 percent; demands are revocable until sufficient demands are received).

[#MBCA702b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.02(b) (sets the default record date for determining shareholders entitled to demand a special meeting and imposes a 60‑day window for collecting sufficient demands).

[#MBCA702c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.02(c) (special meetings may be held at the bylaw‑fixed place or, if none, at the principal office, unless held solely by remote participation under § 7.09(c)).

[#MBCA702d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.02(d) (only business within the purposes stated in the special‑meeting notice may be conducted).

[#MBCA702cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.02 Official Comment (distinguishes annual and special meetings by scope of permissible business; explains shareholder demand mechanics, revocation, and the corporation’s obligation to schedule a timely meeting once a valid demand exists).

[#MBCA703]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.03 (provides a judicial remedy when required shareholder meetings are not held or properly noticed).

[#MBCA703a1]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.03(a)(1) (a court may summarily order an annual meeting on application of any shareholder if one has not been held, nor action by written consent taken, within the earlier of six months after fiscal year‑end or 15 months after the last annual meeting).

[#MBCA703a2]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.03(a)(2) (a court may order a special meeting upon application by one or more demanding shareholders if notice is not given within 30 days after sufficient demands are delivered or the meeting is not held as noticed).

[#MBCA703b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.03(b) (the court may set time and place, fix record dates, prescribe notice contents, alter quorum requirements, and issue other orders needed to accomplish the meeting’s purposes).

[#MBCA703c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.03(c) (for § 7.03(a)(1), “shareholder” includes record shareholders, beneficial shareholders, and unrestricted voting trust beneficial owners).

[#MBCA703cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.03 Official Comment (gives courts broad remedial discretion, including to override normal quorum and notice rules, to prevent managerial obstruction of meetings while allowing denial of repetitive or abusive requests).

[#MBCA704]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04 (authorizes shareholder action by written consent in lieu of a meeting).

[#MBCA704a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04(a) (unanimous written consent by all shareholders entitled to vote may replace a meeting; consents must be dated, describe the action, signed, and delivered for filing with corporate records).

[#MBCA704b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04(b) (the articles may permit non‑unanimous written consents by shareholders holding at least the votes needed to approve the action at a fully attended meeting; directors cannot be elected by non‑unanimous consent if cumulative voting is authorized).

[#MBCA704c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04(c) (fixes default record dates for consent actions, imposes a 60‑day aggregation period for consents, and allows written revocation until sufficient unrevoked consents are delivered).

[#MBCA704d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04(d) (consent has the effect of a vote at a meeting; absent a reasonable tabulation delay authorized by governing documents, effectiveness occurs upon delivery of consents sufficient to take the action).

[#MBCA704e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04(e) (if nonvoting shareholders are entitled to meeting notice for an action to be taken by consent, they must receive equivalent post‑action notice within 10 days after sufficient consents are delivered or tabulation is completed).

[#MBCA704f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04(f) (nonconsenting voting shareholders must similarly receive notice within 10 days after sufficient consents are delivered or tabulation is completed).

[#MBCA704g]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04(g) (failure to give post‑action notices does not delay effectiveness or automatically invalidate the action, but courts may grant remedies to adversely affected shareholders).

[#MBCA704cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.04 Official Comment (recognizes unanimous written consent as a universal alternative to meetings and allows optional non‑unanimous consent; addresses consent form (including electronic signatures), timing, notice to nonconsenting and nonvoting shareholders, and revocation mechanics).

[#MBCA705]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.05 (sets content, timing, and record‑date rules for notices of shareholder meetings).

[#MBCA705a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.05(a) (corporation must give notice of date, time, and place, if any, of each annual and special meeting 10–60 days before the meeting; if remote participation is authorized, the notice must describe the means; notice must include the voting record date if it differs from the notice record date; notice is required only for shareholders entitled to vote, unless law or articles require broader notice).

[#MBCA705b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.05(b) (notice of an annual meeting need not state purposes unless required by the Act or the articles).

[#MBCA705c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.05(c) (notice of a special meeting must state the meeting’s purposes).

[#MBCA705d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.05(d) (default record date for notice and voting, if not otherwise fixed, is the day before the first notice is delivered).

[#MBCA705e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.05(e) (adjourned‑meeting notice is generally unnecessary if the new date, time, and place are announced at the meeting and no new record date is or must be fixed; a new record date triggers fresh notice to new record‑date shareholders).

[#MBCA705cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.05 Official Comment (clarifies interplay between annual‑meeting notice and special statutory notice requirements for fundamental transactions; explains how adjournment interacts with notice, record dates, and quorum, and notes the role of advance‑notice bylaws for shareholder nominations and proposals).

[#MBCA706]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.06 (governs waiver of shareholder notice).

[#MBCA706a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.06(a) (a shareholder may waive notice, before or after the stated meeting time, by a signed written waiver delivered for filing with corporate records).

[#MBCA706b1]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.06(b)(1) (attendance waives objections to lack of notice or defective notice, unless the shareholder objects at the beginning of the meeting to holding the meeting or transacting business).

[#MBCA706b2]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.06(b)(2) (attendance waives objection to considering a matter outside the stated purposes of a special‑meeting notice unless the shareholder objects when the matter is presented).

[#MBCA706cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.06 Official Comment (attendance, including by remote means, generally cures notice defects unless a timely objection is made; the rules force shareholders to raise technical objections promptly rather than holding them in reserve).

[#MBCA707]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.07 (authorizes fixing record dates for meeting‑related actions and regulates their timing and effect).

[#MBCA707a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.07(a) (bylaws, or if they do not so provide, the board, may fix record dates for one or more voting groups to determine shareholders entitled to notice, to demand a special meeting, to vote, or to take other action).

[#MBCA707b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.07(b) (a record date under § 7.07 may not be more than 70 days before the meeting or other action and may not be retroactive).

[#MBCA707c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.07(c) (a record date for a meeting remains effective for adjournments, except that if the meeting is adjourned to a date more than 120 days later, the board must fix a new record date or dates).

[#MBCA707d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.07(d) (if a court orders an adjournment beyond 120 days, it may leave the original record date in place or fix a new one).

[#MBCA707e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.07(e) (a record date fixed for a meeting serves for both notice and voting unless, when fixing the notice record date, the board sets a later voting record date on or before the meeting date, consistent with the bylaws).

[#MBCA707cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.07 Official Comment (permits separate notice and voting record dates to better align voting power with current ownership, especially in public companies, while coordinating with shareholder‑list and information‑access rules).

[#MBCA708]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.08 (addresses conduct and procedural control of shareholder meetings).

[#MBCA708a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.08(a) (a chair must preside at each shareholders’ meeting, appointed under the bylaws or, failing that, by the board).

[#MBCA708b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.08(b) (subject to the articles and bylaws, the chair determines the order of business and may establish rules of conduct for the meeting).

[#MBCA708c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.08(c) (meeting rules and conduct must be fair to shareholders).

[#MBCA708d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.08(d) (the chair must announce when the polls close for each matter; if no announcement is made, polls close at final adjournment; no votes or revocations may be accepted after the polls close).

[#MBCA708cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.08 Official Comment (confirms the chair’s authority to manage orderly, time‑limited debate and recognition of speakers, subject to fairness and to shareholders’ rights under the Act, the articles, and the bylaws).

[#MBCA709]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.09 (authorizes remote participation at shareholder meetings and meetings held solely by remote means).

[#MBCA709a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.09(a) (the board may allow shareholders of any class or series to participate by remote communication pursuant to procedures and guidelines it adopts).

[#MBCA709b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.09(b) (remote participants are deemed present and may vote if the corporation implements reasonable measures to verify their shareholder status and to provide substantially concurrent access to deliberations, communication, and voting).

[#MBCA709c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.09(c) (unless the bylaws require a physical place, the board may decide that a meeting will be held solely by remote means, provided the § 7.09(b) safeguards are satisfied).

[#MBCA709cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.09 Official Comment (enables internet and telephonic meetings, including virtual‑only meetings, without altering existing rules on fairness, order of business, or shareholder participation; permits reasonable procedural conditions on remote participation, including cut‑off dates and minimum participation thresholds).

[#MBCA720]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.20 (requires preparation and shareholder access to lists of shareholders entitled to notice and to vote at a meeting, including electronic contact information when used for meeting‑related communications).

[#MBCA720a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.20(a) (after fixing record dates, the corporation must prepare alphabetical lists, by voting group and class/series, showing names, postal addresses, number and type of shares held, and any email or other electronic address used for meeting notices or communications).

[#MBCA720b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.20(b) (the notice‑entitled list must be available for shareholder inspection from two business days after notice through the meeting, either at the principal office or a stated local place, or on a reasonably accessible electronic network, with access information in the meeting notice; the voting‑entitled list must be similarly available promptly after the voting record date).

[#MBCA720c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.20(c) (a shareholder, or a beneficial owner under § 16.02, may inspect and, subject to § 16.02(c), copy the list during regular business hours at the specified location or electronically, upon written demand made in good faith and for a proper purpose related to the meeting).

[#MBCA720d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.20(d) (if the corporation refuses to make the list available, a court may summarily order inspection or copying at the corporation’s expense and may postpone the meeting until the shareholder’s inspection or copying is complete).

[#MBCA720e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.20(e) (failure to prepare or make available the list does not affect the validity of action taken at the meeting).

[#MBCA720cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.20 Official Comment (the list serves both meeting‑administration and shareholder‑communication functions; use is limited to matters relating to the meeting, and the list‑inspection right is independent of the broader records‑inspection rights under chapter 16).

[#MBCA721]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.21 (defines which shares are entitled to vote and addresses treasury and redeemable shares).

[#MBCA721a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.21(a) (by default, each outstanding share has one vote on each matter, unless the articles provide otherwise; only shares may be vested with voting power).

[#MBCA721b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.21(b) (shares are not entitled to vote if they are owned by, or otherwise belong to, the corporation, directly or indirectly through controlled entities).

[#MBCA721c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.21(c) (shares held by the corporation in a fiduciary capacity for others may vote unless held for the corporation’s own benefit, directly or indirectly through controlled entities).

[#MBCA721d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.21(d) (once notice of redemption is effective and funds sufficient to redeem are deposited with an appropriate financial institution, redeemable shares lose voting rights).

[#MBCA721cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.21 Official Comment (permits flexible allocation of voting power among share classes and series while prohibiting “circular” voting by shares that belong economically to the corporation itself; confirms that nonshareholder securities, such as debt, cannot directly carry voting rights).

[#MBCA722]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22 (governs proxy appointment, duration, revocability, and effect).

[#MBCA722a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(a) (a shareholder may vote in person or by proxy).

[#MBCA722b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(b) (a proxy may be appointed by signed written form or electronic transmission containing date and authorization information sufficient to identify the sender).

[#MBCA722c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(c) (a proxy appointment becomes effective when received by the authorized corporate recipient and, absent a stated term, lasts 11 months).

[#MBCA722d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(d) (a proxy is revocable unless it explicitly states it is irrevocable and is coupled with an interest, such as a pledgee, purchaser, extending creditor, required employee, or party to a voting agreement).

[#MBCA722e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(e) (the shareholder’s death or incapacity does not revoke a proxy until notice is received by the secretary or other tabulating officer or agent before the proxy acts).

[#MBCA722f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(f) (an irrevocable proxy terminates when the coupled interest is extinguished).

[#MBCA722g]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(g) (an irrevocable proxy generally survives share transfers, binding a transferee, except that a good‑faith purchaser for value without knowledge may revoke if the irrevocable proxy was not conspicuously noted on the certificate or information statement).

[#MBCA722h]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22(h) (subject to § 7.24 and any express limitations, the corporation may accept a proxy’s vote or other action as that of the appointing shareholder).

[#MBCA722cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.22 Official Comment (treats proxy appointments as agency arrangements, supports electronic proxy mechanisms, and delineates when “coupled‑with‑an‑interest” proxies are irrevocable and enforceable against transferees).

[#MBCA723]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.23 (facilitates voting and communication where shares are held through intermediaries and nominees).

[#MBCA723a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.23(a) (an intermediary or nominee that is the record shareholder of shares held for others may vote, execute consents, waivers, and demands, and otherwise act as the shareholder, based on beneficial owners’ instructions or, if authorized, without them).

[#MBCA723b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.23(b) (a corporation may establish procedures under which a beneficial owner may become a “shareholder” for Act purposes by filing a beneficial‑ownership certificate, thereby gaining direct rights such as inspection or voting, subject to conditions the corporation sets).

[#MBCA723c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.23(c) (procedures may address certification form, documentary support, notice requirements, duration of status, and other aspects of rights and duties created by beneficial‑ownership certificates).

[#MBCA723cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.23 Official Comment (recognizes modern street‑name and depository systems; permits direct corporation–beneficial owner communication and rights allocation while preserving record‑holder mechanics and UCC intermediated‑holding structures).

[#MBCA724]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.24 (sets standards for corporate acceptance or rejection of votes, consents, waivers, demands, and proxy appointments).

[#MBCA724a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.24(a) (if the signature on a vote, consent, waiver, demand, or proxy corresponds to the shareholder’s name, the corporation may in good faith accept and treat it as that shareholder’s act).

[#MBCA724b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.24(b) (if the signature does not match the shareholder’s name, the corporation may still, in good faith, accept it as the shareholder’s act if it appears to be that of: (1) an officer or agent of an entity shareholder; (2) a fiduciary such as an executor or guardian (with requested proof); (3) a receiver or bankruptcy trustee (with requested proof); (4) a pledgee, beneficial owner, or attorney‑in‑fact (with requested proof); or (5) another person reasonably believed authorized to sign for the shareholder).

[#MBCA724c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.24(c) (the corporation may reject a purported shareholder act if the authorized officer or agent has a reasonable basis for doubt about its validity).

[#MBCA724d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.24(d) (corporate good‑faith acceptance or rejection of such instruments is protected against claims based on invalidity; this does not limit legal claims against the instrument’s signer or the proxy under other law).

[#MBCA724e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.24(e) (if an inspector of election is appointed, the inspector’s determinations regarding acceptance or rejection of votes and related instruments control over conflicting corporate views).

[#MBCA724cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.24 Official Comment (gives corporations and inspectors practical safe harbors for relying on facially valid instruments, while leaving underlying agency disputes and proxy‑holder liability to general law and allowing corporations to adopt supplemental evidentiary guidelines).

[#MBCA725]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25 (establishes default quorum and voting rules for shareholder voting groups and ties them to any supermajority requirements in the articles).

[#MBCA725a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25(a) (a voting group may act at a meeting only if a quorum of that group exists; by default, a quorum is shares representing a majority of votes entitled to be cast; article‑level quorum reductions below Act‑specified minima are prohibited).

[#MBCA725b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25(b) (once represented for any purpose, shares are deemed present for quorum for the remainder of the meeting and any adjournment, unless a new record date is set).

[#MBCA725c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25(c) (if a quorum exists, action other than director elections is approved if votes cast in favor exceed votes cast against, unless the articles require more).

[#MBCA725d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25(d) (amendments adding, changing, or deleting higher‑than‑default quorum or voting requirements are governed by § 7.27).

[#MBCA725e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25(e) (director elections are governed by § 7.28).

[#MBCA725f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25(f) (when the Act grants separate voting‑group rights, the grouping rules in § 10.04(c) apply, including board authority to aggregate similarly affected classes and series unless the articles or the Act provide otherwise).

[#MBCA725cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.25 Official Comment (defines “voting group,” explains that abstentions do not count as votes cast, and discusses how different quorum and voting thresholds can apply to different matters or groups within a single meeting).

[#MBCA726]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.26 (sets the basic rule for when action is taken by one or multiple voting groups).

[#MBCA726a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.26(a) (if only one voting group is entitled to vote on a matter, action is taken when that group acts in accordance with § 7.25).

[#MBCA726b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.26(b) (if two or more voting groups are entitled to vote, action is taken only when each group votes separately and satisfies § 7.25; groups may act at different times).

[#MBCA726cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.26 Official Comment (explains how multi‑group votes work, including situations where one group can proceed on matters not requiring action by other groups, and cases where a class participates in both a general voting group and a separate class‑vote group).

[#MBCA727]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.27 (protects supermajority and special quorum requirements by imposing “locked‑in” approval thresholds for amendments that would change them).

[#MBCA727a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.27 (an amendment adding, changing, or deleting a quorum or voting requirement must itself satisfy both the existing and the proposed requirements, including applicable voting‑group thresholds, and must be approved by the greater of the two).

[#MBCA727cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.27 Official Comment (prevents dilution of entrenched quorum and supermajority provisions without meeting their own standards; describes how to apply this rule when both quorum and voting requirements are being changed).

[#MBCA728]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.28 (sets default plurality voting for director elections and provides an opt‑in framework for cumulative voting).

[#MBCA728a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.28(a) (unless the articles provide otherwise, directors are elected by a plurality of votes cast by shares entitled to vote at a meeting with a quorum).

[#MBCA728b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.28(b) (shareholders have no cumulative‑voting rights unless the articles affirmatively provide for them).

[#MBCA728c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.28(c) (a cumulative‑voting provision entitles designated shareholders to multiply votes by the number of directors to be elected and allocate the product among one or more candidates).

[#MBCA728d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.28(d) (cumulative voting may be used at a meeting only if (1) the notice or proxy statement conspicuously states that cumulative voting is authorized, or (2) a shareholder entitled to cumulate gives the corporation notice at least 48 hours before the meeting, which then allows all shareholders in that voting group to cumulate).

[#MBCA728cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.28 Official Comment (explains plurality elections, interaction with staggered boards and voting groups, mechanics of cumulative voting, and the rule that directors cannot be elected by less‑than‑unanimous written consent where cumulative voting is authorized).

[#MBCA729]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.29 (authorizes appointment and defines duties and powers of inspectors of election).

[#MBCA729a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.29(a) (a corporation with equity securities registered under Exchange Act § 12 must appoint one or more inspectors for shareholder meetings; other corporations may do so in their bylaws or by board or chair action).

[#MBCA729b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.29(b) (inspectors may be officers, employees, agents, or independent persons of integrity and must certify their determinations).

[#MBCA729c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.29(c) (inspectors determine the number of shares outstanding, the voting power of each, the shares represented at the meeting, validity and effect of proxies and ballots, and the results of votes, and may examine relevant records and receive evidence).

[#MBCA729d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.29(d) (inspectors act impartially and in good faith; their determinations are prima facie evidence of the facts stated).

[#MBCA729e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.29(e) (if an inspector’s appointment is challenged, the court may appoint a replacement or additional inspector and define that inspector’s authority).

[#MBCA729cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.29 Official Comment (supports reliable tabulation and dispute resolution in contested elections and votes; coordinates inspector authority with § 7.24’s standards on accepting or rejecting proxies and ballots).

[#MBCA730]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.30 (authorizes voting trusts and sets minimal formation and disclosure requirements).

[#MBCA730a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.30(a) (one or more shareholders may create a voting trust by signing a trust agreement, transferring shares to the trustee, and having the trustee deliver to the corporation at its principal office a copy of the agreement and a list of beneficial owners, their addresses, and the number and class of shares transferred).

[#MBCA730b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.30(b) (a voting trust becomes effective when the first shares are registered in the trustee’s name).

[#MBCA730c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.30(c) (any limits on the duration of a voting trust are as stated in the trust; legacy voting trusts formed under a former 10‑year limit remain subject to that prior duration regime unless unanimously amended).

[#MBCA730cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.30 Official Comment (describes voting trusts as pooling voting power in trustees while preserving beneficial ownership; allows highly flexible trust terms and confirms that modern Act practice imposes no default duration limit, in contrast to earlier 10‑year caps).

[#MBCA731]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.31 (recognizes contract‑based shareholder voting agreements independent of voting‑trust rules).

[#MBCA731a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.31(a) (two or more shareholders may sign an agreement specifying how they will vote their shares; such agreements are not subject to § 7.30).

[#MBCA731b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.31(b) (a voting agreement is specifically enforceable).

[#MBCA731cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.31 Official Comment (treats voting agreements as ordinary contracts requiring a signed writing; notes that enforcement may occur via appointed proxies made irrevocable under § 7.22 and that damages are typically inadequate, making specific performance the appropriate remedy).

[#MBCA732]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32 (validates broad shareholder‑level governance agreements, even when they depart from default Act norms).

[#MBCA732a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(a) (a compliant shareholder agreement is effective among shareholders and the corporation even if inconsistent with the Act, and may: (1) eliminate or constrain the board; (2) govern distributions, subject to § 6.40; (3) fix directors’ or officers’ identity, terms, or selection/removal; (4) reallocate voting power among shareholders and directors; (5) set terms for intra‑firm contracts; (6) transfer managerial authority to shareholders or others, including deadlock‑breaking; (7) require dissolution upon specified events; or (8) otherwise govern corporate powers, management, or internal relationships, so long as not contrary to public policy).

[#MBCA732b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(b) (the agreement must either be set forth in the articles or bylaws and unanimously approved by current shareholders, or be in a written instrument signed by all current shareholders and made known to the corporation; amendment generally requires unanimity unless the agreement provides otherwise).

[#MBCA732c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(c) (existence of the agreement must be conspicuously noted on share certificates or on the § 6.26(b) information statement for uncertificated shares; failure to note does not affect validity but gives a purchaser without knowledge a rescission right, subject to brief limitations periods).

[#MBCA732d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(d) (if the agreement ceases to be effective, the board may, without shareholder action, amend the articles or bylaws to delete it and related references).

[#MBCA732e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(e) (to the extent an agreement shifts or limits board discretion or powers, it correspondingly relieves directors of related liabilities and imposes them on the persons in whom such powers are vested).

[#MBCA732f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(f) (neither the existence nor performance of a § 7.32 agreement, even if it causes partnership‑like operation or informality, creates personal shareholder liability for corporate acts or debts).

[#MBCA732g]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(g) (incorporators or subscribers may act as shareholders for purposes of a § 7.32 agreement before shares are issued).

[#MBCA732h]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32(h) (any duration limits must be stated in the agreement; legacy agreements formed under a former 10‑year default term remain governed by that earlier duration rule unless the agreement then allowed amendment).

[#MBCA732cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.32 Official Comment (positions § 7.32 as a flexible close‑corporation‑style contracting provision; stresses unanimity and notice to protect later purchasers, preserves non‑overridable public‑policy constraints, and clarifies that transferees remain bound but may have rescission or damages remedies in appropriate cases).

[#MBCA740]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.40 (defines key terms for derivative‑proceeding rules).

[#MBCA740def]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.40 (in subchapter D, “derivative proceeding” means a civil suit in the right of the corporation, domestic or certain foreign, to recover for corporate injury; “shareholder” includes record shareholders, beneficial shareholders, and unrestricted voting‑trust beneficial owners).

[#MBCA740cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.40 Official Comment (distinguishes derivative from direct claims, emphasizes that recovery runs to the corporation in derivative suits, and explains why beneficial owners and certain trust beneficiaries receive standing for derivative purposes).

[#MBCA741]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.41 (sets standing requirements for derivative plaintiffs).

[#MBCA741text]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.41 (a shareholder may not commence or maintain a derivative proceeding unless (i) the shareholder held shares at the time of the challenged act or omission, or acquired them by operation of law from someone who did, and (ii) the shareholder fairly and adequately represents the corporation’s interests in enforcing its right).

[#MBCA741cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.41 Official Comment (codifies contemporaneous‑ownership and adequate‑representation requirements; notes that loss of shareholder status generally ends standing, subject to narrow exceptions such as mergers engineered to extinguish derivative claims).

[#MBCA742]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.42 (requires a written demand on the corporation before initiating a derivative proceeding).

[#MBCA742text]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.42 (no derivative proceeding may commence until a written demand is delivered to the corporation requesting suitable action and 90 days have passed, unless the corporation rejects the demand earlier or waiting would cause irreparable injury; the demand must detail reasons, requested action, and state the possibility of a derivative suit, and a beneficial owner must supply evidence of ownership).

[#MBCA742cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.42 Official Comment (adopts a universal‑demand rule to avoid litigating demand‑futility; characterizes the 90‑day period as modest and notes that it may be shortened where delay risks irreparable harm).

[#MBCA743]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.43 (permits courts to stay derivative proceedings while the corporation investigates the demand).

[#MBCA743text]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.43 (if the corporation initiates an inquiry into the allegations in the demand or complaint, the court may stay the derivative proceeding for a period it deems appropriate).

[#MBCA743cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.43 Official Comment (a stay is often appropriate when a complaint is filed at or shortly after the 90‑day mark but the corporation’s good‑faith investigation is ongoing; courts are expected to monitor the inquiry’s progress and fairness).

[#MBCA744]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.44 (governs dismissal of derivative proceedings based on a corporation’s internal determination that continuation is not in the corporation’s best interests).

[#MBCA744a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.44(a) (on the corporation’s motion, a court must dismiss a derivative proceeding if, after a reasonable, good‑faith inquiry, a specified decision‑making body concludes that maintenance of the proceeding is not in the corporation’s best interests).

[#MBCA744b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.44(b) (the determination must be made by: (1) a majority of qualified directors constituting a quorum; (2) a committee of two or more qualified directors appointed by qualified directors; or (3) a court‑appointed panel of one or more individuals, on the corporation’s motion).

[#MBCA744c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.44(c) (to contest such a determination, the plaintiff must plead with particularity facts showing that § 7.44(a)’s requirements were not met).

[#MBCA744d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.44(d) (allocates the burden of proof: if the determination was by qualified directors or a qualified‑director committee, the plaintiff generally bears the burden unless particularized allegations show that a majority of the board was not qualified; if by a court‑appointed panel, the corporation bears the burden).

[#MBCA744e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.44(e) (the court may require that any § 7.44(a) dismissal motion be made within a reasonable specified time).

[#MBCA744cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.44 Official Comment (describes how qualified directors or panels investigate and decide derivative demands; clarifies that courts review process, good faith, and logical connection between inquiry and conclusions rather than second‑guessing business judgment on litigation strategy).

[#MBCA745]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.45 (requires court approval for discontinuance or settlement of derivative proceedings and, when interests of shareholders may be substantially affected, mandates notice to affected shareholders or classes).

[#MBCA745cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.45 Official Comment (emphasizes that derivative suits are brought for the corporation’s benefit, not as private actions; explains that courts may waive notice for frivolous or moot cases and retain discretion over who bears notice costs and how notice is given).

[#MBCA746]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.46 (authorizes fee‑shifting and cost awards at the conclusion of derivative proceedings).

[#MBCA7461]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.46(1) (the court may order the corporation to pay the plaintiff’s expenses if the proceeding results in a substantial benefit to the corporation).

[#MBCA7462]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.46(2) (the court may order the plaintiff to pay the corporation’s or any defendant’s expenses if the demand or proceeding was made, commenced, or maintained without reasonable cause or for an improper purpose).

[#MBCA7463]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.46(3) (the court may order a party to pay another party’s expenses incurred because of filings or tactics not in good faith, not warranted by existing law or a nonfrivolous argument to change it, or for improper purposes such as harassment or needless cost).

[#MBCA746cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.46 Official Comment (explains “substantial benefit” and aligns the sanctions standard with, but not identical to, rules addressing abuse of litigation; notes that expenses may include fees of qualified directors and special litigation committees).

[#MBCA747]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.47 (sets choice‑of‑law rules for derivative proceedings involving foreign corporations).

[#MBCA747text]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.47 (in derivative proceedings on behalf of a foreign corporation, matters covered by subchapter D are governed by the foreign jurisdiction’s law, except that §§ 7.43, 7.45, and 7.46 are governed by the forum state’s law).

[#MBCA747cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.47 Official Comment (reserves core governance issues for the incorporating jurisdiction while ensuring the forum court retains control over procedural matters such as stays, settlements, and expense shifting).

[#MBCA748]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48 (allows shareholders to seek court appointment of a custodian or, if the corporation is insolvent, a receiver).

[#MBCA748a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48(a) (on a shareholder’s action, a court may appoint a custodian or, if insolvent, a receiver when (1) directors are deadlocked, shareholders cannot break the deadlock, and irreparable injury is threatened or occurring, or (2) directors or controllers are acting fraudulently and irreparable injury is threatened or occurring).

[#MBCA748b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48(b) (the court may issue interim remedies, must provide notice and a full hearing before final appointment, and has jurisdiction over the corporation and all its property).

[#MBCA748c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48(c) (custodians or receivers may be individuals or qualified corporations and may be required to post bond).

[#MBCA748d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48(d) (the appointing order defines powers and duties, which may include: (1) for custodians, exercising corporate powers in place of the board to manage the business; (2) for receivers, disposing of assets with court approval and litigating in their own name).

[#MBCA748e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48(e) (the court may redesignate a custodian as receiver or vice versa as circumstances change).

[#MBCA748f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48(f) (the court may order compensation and reimbursement of expenses for the custodian or receiver from corporate assets).

[#MBCA748g]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48(g) (for § 7.48 purposes, “shareholder” includes record shareholders, beneficial shareholders, and unrestricted voting‑trust beneficial owners).

[#MBCA748cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.48 Official Comment (positions custodianship/receivership as a narrow, irreparable‑injury remedy distinct from judicial dissolution; highlights its availability as an alternative to dissolution for nonpublic corporations and its extension to certain beneficial owners).

[#MBCA749]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.49 (provides a judicial mechanism to resolve disputes over corporate offices, elections, and shareholder votes).

[#MBCA749a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.49(a) (on application of eligible persons, a court may determine: (1) validity or result of director/officer elections, appointments, removals, or resignations; (2) an individual’s right to hold such offices; (3) validity or result of any shareholder vote; (4) a director’s right to committee membership; and (5) rights to nominate or be nominated as a director, including rights under bylaws adopted under § 2.06(c) or comparable provisions).

[#MBCA749b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.49(b) (standing to seek relief extends to specified parties such as the corporation, directors, officers, and shareholders; details are in the section text).

[#MBCA749c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.49(c) (the court may order new elections, direct how votes must be counted, resolve nomination‑rule disputes, or grant other appropriate relief to protect corporate and shareholder interests).

[#MBCA749cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 7.49 Official Comment (creates a focused, flexible remedy for election and voting disputes, intended to complement but not displace other corporate and securities‑law mechanisms regulating proxy contests and voting procedures).



[#MBCA801]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.01 (board requirement and allocation of corporate powers).

[#MBCA801a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.01(a) (each corporation must have board of directors unless dispensed with under section 7.32).

[#MBCA801b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.01(b) (corporate powers exercised by or under board authority; business managed by or under board direction, subject to articles or section 7.32 agreement).

[#MBCA801cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.01 Official Comment (board as central governance body with delegation authority; oversight role in public companies).

[#MBCA802]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.02 (qualifications of directors and director nominees).

[#MBCA802a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.02(a) (articles or bylaws may prescribe director qualifications).

[#MBCA802b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.02(b) (qualification based on viewpoint or opinion that limits duty discharge not permitted; disqualification based on sanctions or court order permitted).

[#MBCA802c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.02(c) (director need not be resident or shareholder unless articles or bylaws require).

[#MBCA802d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.02(d) (pre-nomination qualification must exist before individual becomes nominee; later-adopted qualification inapplicable to existing nominees).

[#MBCA802e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.02(e) (in-service qualification may be imposed prospectively; does not apply until start of next term for sitting directors).

[#MBCA802cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.02 Official Comment (permissible qualifications include residency, ownership, experience; timing rules prevent mid-term disqualification).

[#MBCA803]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.03 (number and election of directors).

[#MBCA803a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.03(a) (board consists of one or more individuals; number specified in or fixed by articles or bylaws).

[#MBCA803b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.03(b) (board size may be changed by articles or bylaws amendment).

[#MBCA803c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.03(c) (directors elected at first and each subsequent annual meeting unless staggered under section 8.06).

[#MBCA803cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.03 Official Comment (methods for fixing board size; control implications in close corporations).

[#MBCA804]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.04 (election of directors by certain classes or series of shareholders).

[#MBCA804]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.04 (articles may authorize class or series to elect specific directors; each such group constitutes separate voting group).

[#MBCA804cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.04 Official Comment (class-based election rights allocate board representation among investor groups).

[#MBCA805]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.05 (terms of directors generally).

[#MBCA805]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.05 (director terms expire at next annual meeting unless staggered; holdover until successor qualifies unless section 10.22 truncation applies).

[#MBCA805cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.05 Official Comment (interaction of term structures with vacancies and holdover service).

[#MBCA806]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.06 (staggered terms for directors).

[#MBCA806]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.06 (articles may divide board into two or three groups with staggered multi-year terms).

[#MBCA806cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.06 Official Comment (staggered boards require articles provision; effects on control contests and removal).

[#MBCA807]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.07 (resignation of directors).

[#MBCA807a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.07(a) (director may resign by written notice to board, chair, or secretary).

[#MBCA807b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.07(b) (resignation effective when received unless notice specifies later date or condition; conditioned resignation may be irrevocable).

[#MBCA807cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.07 Official Comment (authorizes contingent and delayed resignations; supports majority-vote director election practices).

[#MBCA808]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.08 (removal of directors by shareholders).

[#MBCA808a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.08(a) (shareholders may remove directors with or without cause unless articles require cause).

[#MBCA808b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.08(b) (only electing voting group may participate in removal vote).

[#MBCA808c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.08(c) (director removed if votes to remove exceed votes against; cumulative-voting protection applies).

[#MBCA808d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.08(d) (removal only at meeting called for that purpose; notice must state removal purpose).

[#MBCA808cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.08 Official Comment (at-will removal default; protects cumulative-voting minorities; judicial removal under section 8.09 available).

[#MBCA809]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.09 (removal of directors by judicial proceeding).

[#MBCA809a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.09(a) (court may remove director for fraudulent, intentional criminal, or grossly abusive conduct if removal in corporation's best interests).

[#MBCA809b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.09(b) (shareholder removal proceeding subject to subchapter 7D procedures except contemporaneous-ownership requirement).

[#MBCA809cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.09 Official Comment (judicial removal as extraordinary remedy for egregious misconduct when shareholder removal impracticable).

[#MBCA810]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.10 (vacancy on board of directors).

[#MBCA810a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.10(a) (vacancy may be filled by shareholders, by board, or by remaining directors if fewer than quorum, unless articles provide otherwise).

[#MBCA810b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.10(b) (voting-group vacancy filled only by that voting group or directors elected by that group).

[#MBCA810c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.10(c) (future vacancy may be filled in advance but new director takes office only when vacancy occurs).

[#MBCA810cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.10 Official Comment (less-than-quorum filling authority; preserves voting-group representation).

[#MBCA811]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.11 (compensation of directors).

[#MBCA811]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.11 (board may fix director compensation unless articles or bylaws provide otherwise).

[#MBCA811cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.11 Official Comment (director compensation governed by conflicting-interest transaction rules in subchapter 8F).


[#MBCA820]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.20 (meetings of board).

[#MBCA820a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.20(a) (board may hold meetings in or out of state).

[#MBCA820b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.20(b) (directors may participate by remote communication if all can simultaneously hear each other; such participation constitutes presence).

[#MBCA821]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.21 (action by directors without meeting).

[#MBCA821a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.21(a) (board may act by unanimous written consent unless articles or bylaws require meeting).

[#MBCA821b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.21(b) (action effective when all consents received unless consent specifies later date; consent revocable before all signatures obtained).

[#MBCA821c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.21(c) (consent has effect of meeting action).

[#MBCA822]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.22 (notice of meetings).

[#MBCA822a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.22(a) (regular meetings may be held without notice unless articles or bylaws require).

[#MBCA822b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.22(b) (special meetings require at least two days' notice of date, time, and place unless articles or bylaws specify different period).

[#MBCA823]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.23 (waiver of notice).

[#MBCA823a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.23(a) (director may waive notice in writing before or after meeting).

[#MBCA823b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.23(b) (attendance waives notice unless director objects at start and does not vote for action).

[#MBCA824]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.24 (quorum and voting).

[#MBCA824a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.24(a) (quorum is majority of fixed board size unless articles, bylaws, or Act provide otherwise).

[#MBCA824b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.24(b) (quorum may not be less than one-third of fixed board size).

[#MBCA824c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.24(c) (if quorum present, majority of directors present is board act unless greater vote required).

[#MBCA824d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.24(d) (director present deemed to assent unless objecting at start, dissent entered in minutes, or written notice of dissent delivered).

[#MBCA825]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.25 (committees of the board).

[#MBCA825a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.25(a) (board may create committees of one or more directors to perform board functions unless Act, articles, or bylaws prohibit).

[#MBCA825b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.25(b) (committee creation requires majority vote of all directors or higher threshold in articles or bylaws).

[#MBCA825c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.25(c) (sections 8.20 through 8.24 apply to committees).

[#MBCA825d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.25(d) (committee powers specified by resolution; committees may not authorize distributions except by formula, approve shareholder-submitted matters, fill board vacancies subject to subsection (e), or adopt, amend, or repeal bylaws).

[#MBCA825e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.25(e) (alternate committee members may be appointed; remaining non-disqualified members may unanimously appoint substitute during absence or disqualification).

[#MBCA826]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.26 (submission of matters for shareholder vote).

[#MBCA826]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.26 (corporation may agree to submit matter to shareholders even if board later withdraws recommendation).

[#MBCA826cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.26 Official Comment (validates submission commitments despite recommendation changes; does not alter director conduct standards).


[#MBCA830]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.30 (standards of conduct for directors).

[#MBCA830a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.30(a) (director must act in good faith and in manner director reasonably believes in corporation's best interests).

[#MBCA830b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.30(b) (director must discharge decision-making and oversight duties with care appropriate under the circumstances).

[#MBCA830c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.30(c) (business judgment presumed met if director not financially interested, informed to extent reasonably believed appropriate, and rationally believes judgment in best interests).

[#MBCA830d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.30(d) (director may rely on officers, employees, experts, and committees if reliance reasonable and director lacks knowledge making reliance unwarranted).

[#MBCA830cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.30 Official Comment (distinguishes conduct standards from liability standards; addresses decision-making, oversight, disclosure, and reliance).

[#MBCA831]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.31 (standards of liability for directors).

[#MBCA831a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.31(a) (director not liable unless no exculpation provision applies and conduct involved bad faith, uninformed decision, lack of objectivity or independence, sustained oversight failure, or improper financial benefit).

[#MBCA831b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.31(b) (party seeking liability must prove harm and proximate cause for damages; other theories have their own burdens).

[#MBCA831c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.31(c) (section does not alter fairness burdens, other defenses, indemnification rights, or rights under other statutes).

[#MBCA831cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.31 Official Comment (interacts with charter exculpation, indemnification, and safe harbors for conflicting-interest and opportunity cases; proximate-cause requirement).

[#MBCA832]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.32 (directors' liability for unlawful distributions).

[#MBCA832a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.32(a) (director who votes for unlawful distribution personally liable for excess amount if director failed to meet section 8.30 standards).

[#MBCA832b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.32(b) (liable director entitled to contribution from other liable directors and recoupment from knowing shareholders).

[#MBCA832c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.32(c) (liability action barred unless commenced within two years of distribution; contribution or recoupment barred unless commenced within one year of final adjudication).

[#MBCA832cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.32 Official Comment (unlawful-distribution liability tied to section 8.30 breach; equitable allocation among directors and knowing recipients).

[#MBCA833]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.33 (directors' liability for corporate opportunities).

[#MBCA833]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.33 (corporate opportunity taking governed by section 8.70 rather than section 8.31).


[#MBCA840]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.40 (officers).

[#MBCA840a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.40(a) (corporation has officers as described in bylaws or appointed by board).

[#MBCA840b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.40(b) (board elects officers; officer may appoint other officers if authorized).

[#MBCA840c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.40(c) (bylaws or board must assign record-maintenance and authentication responsibility to an officer).

[#MBCA840d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.40(d) (individual may hold multiple offices simultaneously).

[#MBCA840cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.40 Official Comment (flexible officer structure; identifies statutory secretary role; authentication allows third-party reliance).

[#MBCA841]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.41 (functions of officers).

[#MBCA841]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.41 (officer has authority and performs functions in bylaws or prescribed by board or delegating officer).

[#MBCA841cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.41 Official Comment (officer authority may be express, implied, apparent, or ratified; ratification limited to originally authorizable acts).

[#MBCA842]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.42 (standards of conduct for officers).

[#MBCA842a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.42(a) (officer must act in good faith, with appropriate care, and in manner officer reasonably believes in corporation's best interests).

[#MBCA842b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.42(b) (officer must inform superior and CEO or board of material information and violations within officer's knowledge and function scope).

[#MBCA842c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.42(c) (officer may rely on other officers, employees, committees, and experts if reasonable).

[#MBCA842d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.42(d) (officer not liable if duties complied with in good faith; liability determined under applicable law including section 8.31 principles).

[#MBCA842cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.42 Official Comment (officer disclosure obligations; reliance standards; review parallels section 8.31 including business-judgment concepts).

[#MBCA843]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.43 (resignation and removal of officers).

[#MBCA843a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.43(a) (officer may resign by written notice; resignation does not affect contract rights).

[#MBCA843b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.43(b) (resignation may specify delayed effective date or condition; board may fill pending vacancy and may remove officer before effective date).

[#MBCA843c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.43(c) (board or appointing officer may remove any officer with or without cause; removal does not affect contract rights).

[#MBCA843cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.43 Official Comment (at-will removal coexists with employment contracts yielding damages but not reinstatement).

[#MBCA844]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.44 (contract rights of officers).

[#MBCA844a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.44(a) (appointment alone does not create contract rights).

[#MBCA844b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.44(b) (removal does not affect officer's contract rights; resignation does not affect corporation's contract rights).

[#MBCA844cmt]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.44 Official Comment (removal without prejudice to damages claim; premature resignation may breach contract).


[#MBCA850]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.50 (subchapter definitions).

[#MBCA850]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.50 (defines corporation, director, expenses, liability, official capacity, party, and proceeding for indemnification purposes).

[#MBCA851]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.51 (permissible indemnification).

[#MBCA851a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.51(a) (corporation may indemnify director who acted in good faith, believed conduct in or not opposed to corporation's best interests, and had no reason to believe conduct unlawful, or for whom articles authorize broader indemnification under section 2.02(b)(5)).

[#MBCA851b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.51(b) (conduct regarding benefit plans deemed not opposed to corporate interests if director believed conduct in participants' interests).

[#MBCA851c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.51(c) (termination of proceeding not determinative that standard met).

[#MBCA851d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.51(d) (indemnification prohibited in derivative suits except for expenses, and for any proceeding where director received improper financial benefit, unless court orders otherwise).

[#MBCA852]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.52 (mandatory indemnification).

[#MBCA852]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.52 (corporation must indemnify director wholly successful in defense for expenses incurred; director may apply to enforce).

[#MBCA853]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.53 (advance for expenses).

[#MBCA853a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.53(a) (corporation may advance expenses if director provides undertaking to repay and affirms good-faith belief in meeting conduct standards or exculpation coverage).

[#MBCA853b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.53(b) (undertaking is unlimited, unsecured, and accepted without inquiry into financial ability).

[#MBCA853c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.53(c) (advancement authorized by qualified directors or shareholders; disqualified shares may not vote).

[#MBCA853d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.53(d) (authorization required for each specific instance).

[#MBCA853e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.53(e) (advancement right, once granted, not affected by later amendments or director's ceasing service).

[#MBCA854]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.54 (court-ordered indemnification and advance for expenses).

[#MBCA854a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.54(a) (court may order indemnification or advancement if director entitled under sections 8.52, 8.58, or if fairly and reasonably entitled in view of circumstances).

[#MBCA854b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.54(b) (court must order corporation to pay director's litigation expenses if entitled under subsection (a)(1) or (a)(2); may order payment under subsection (a)(3)).

[#MBCA855]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.55 (determination and authorization of indemnification).

[#MBCA855a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.55(a) (permissive indemnification requires prior determination that director met conduct standards).

[#MBCA855b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.55(b) (determination made by qualified directors, special legal counsel, or shareholders excluding disqualified shares).

[#MBCA855c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.55(c) (if fewer than two qualified directors, special counsel selected by board or non-qualified directors).

[#MBCA855d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.55(d) (authorization made same way as determination; if by special counsel, authorization by those who selected counsel).

[#MBCA856]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.56 (indemnification of officers).

[#MBCA856a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.56(a) (officer indemnified and advanced under this subchapter to same extent as director).

[#MBCA856b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.56(b) (officer who is not director entitled to mandatory indemnification and court application to same extent as director).

[#MBCA856c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.56(c) (non-director officer entitled to seek indemnification as authorized by corporation under section 8.58 without limitations in sections 8.51(d) or 8.52(d)).

[#MBCA856d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.56(d) (subsection (c) does not limit indemnification or advancement for non-directors).

[#MBCA857]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.57 (insurance).

[#MBCA857]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.57 (corporation may purchase D&O insurance covering directors and officers regardless of corporation's power to indemnify).

[#MBCA858]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.58 (variation by corporate action; application of subchapter).

[#MBCA858a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.58(a) (corporation may obligate itself in advance to indemnify or advance expenses; obligatory advancement provision deemed included unless provision states otherwise).

[#MBCA858b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.58(b) (advance provision may not obligate for prior action or violate undertaking; may impose conditions including repayment).

[#MBCA858c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.58(c) (corporation may obligate advance expense payment to directors, provide indemnification or advancement to officers and employees, or expand or limit director indemnification beyond statute).

[#MBCA858d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.58(d) (provisions authorized by this section do not require shareholder approval).

[#MBCA859]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.59 (exclusivity of subchapter).

[#MBCA859a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.59(a) (director indemnification and advancement permitted only as provided by this subchapter).

[#MBCA859b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.59(b) (non-director indemnification and advancement permitted as authorized by articles, bylaws, board action, or contract; may extend to same extent as for directors without subchapter limitations).

[#MBCA859c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.59(c) (subchapter does not preclude additional indemnification rights under articles, bylaws, resolutions, contracts, or other law, but articles may impose express prohibitions or limitations).


[#MBCA860]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (subchapter definitions).

[#MBCA860]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (defines conflicting interest, director's conflicting interest transaction, control, material financial interest, fair to corporation, related person, relevant time, and required disclosure for subchapter F).

[#MBCA860defCIT]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (director's conflicting interest transaction means transaction to which director or related person is party or has interest that could influence director's judgment if called to vote).

[#MBCA860defControl]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (control means power to elect entity's directors or managing authority, serve as general partner, or direct entity's management and policies).

[#MBCA860defFair]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (fair to corporation means transaction reasonable in proportion to needs, on arm's-length terms, and no conflicted director improperly influences decision or remains involved post-transaction).

[#MBCA860defMFI]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (material financial interest means interest that would reasonably influence director's vote or judgment on transaction).

[#MBCA860defRelated]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (related person includes director's family, household members, trusts, entities with substantial relationships, and affiliates of such entities).

[#MBCA860defRelevant]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (relevant time means when directors act and, for advance authorization, when corporation becomes legally committed).

[#MBCA860defRequired]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.60 (required disclosure means disclosing existence and nature of conflicting interest and all material facts ordinary director would need).

[#MBCA861]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.61 (judicial action).

[#MBCA861a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.61(a) (conflicting interest transaction protected from challenge if approved by qualified directors under section 8.62, approved by qualified shareholders under section 8.63, or proven fair to corporation).

[#MBCA861b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.61(b) (unreasonable delay or failure to act or disclose does not constitute action for safe-harbor purposes).

[#MBCA861c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.61(c) (section does not alter fairness burdens, other liability limitations, or indemnification rights).

[#MBCA861d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.61(d) (section excludes compensation patterns, dual-directorship transactions, judicially-approved compensation, and chapter 9 transactions absent conduct or public-policy violation).

[#MBCA862]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.62 (directors' action).

[#MBCA862a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.62(a) (qualified-director approval effective if majority of at least two qualified directors vote after required disclosure; entire board may appoint qualified-director committee if no qualified directors on board).

[#MBCA862b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.62(b) (action not ineffective merely because conflicted director's presence required for or counted toward quorum).

[#MBCA862c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.62(c) (failure to disclose information conflicted director unaware of does not invalidate vote if required disclosure made and additional requested information provided).

[#MBCA862d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.62(d) (advance authorization requires notice of conflict and qualified-director action before legal commitment; applies only to facts fully disclosed or unchanged).

[#MBCA863]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.63 (shareholders' action).

[#MBCA863a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.63(a) (shareholder approval effective if majority of qualified shares vote in favor after notice and information provision).

[#MBCA863b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.63(b) (conflicted director must inform vote tabulator of non-qualified shares; failure does not affect validity if unintentional and did not determine outcome).

[#MBCA863c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.63(c) (qualified shares exclude shares beneficially owned or controlled by conflicted director or related person).

[#MBCA863d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.63(d) (majority requirement satisfied by majority of qualified shares).

[#MBCA863e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.63(e) (conflicted director vote does not void action if required disclosure made and vote not counted).

[#MBCA863f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.63(f) (failure to satisfy this section does not prevent fairness showing under section 8.61(a)(3)).


[#MBCA870]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.70 (business opportunities).

[#MBCA870a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.70(a) (director may take disclaimed opportunity if advance disclaimer covers opportunity and remains in effect, or specific disclaimer communicated before director becomes obligated).

[#MBCA870b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.70(b) (corporation has burden to prove opportunity was corporate and disclaimer conditions unmet; if met, person taking opportunity must prove fairness).

[#MBCA870c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.70(c) (advance disclaimer may be specific or categorical; imposed by articles, bylaws, qualified-director policy, or shareholder policy).

[#MBCA870d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.70(d) (officer disclaimer requires qualified-director authorization after required disclosure and periodic ratification without conflicted-director participation).

[#MBCA870e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 8.70(e) (qualified director defined by section 1.43(a)(5); disclaimers do not excuse duties of good faith, fair dealing, disclosure, or avoid using corporate property or information, harming corporation, or acting inconsistently with best interests).



[#MBCA901]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.01 (chapter 9 definitions).

[#MBCA901]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.01 (defines domestication, conversion, domesticating and domesticated corporations, converting and converted entities, protected agreement, and enactment date for chapter 9).

[#MBCA901protected]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.01 (protected agreement means specified pre-enactment debt documents, binding agreements, organic documents, and governance agreements; merger-trigger provisions in protected agreements extended to domestications and conversions).

[#MBCA902]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.02 (excluded transactions).

[#MBCA902]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.02 (optional provision allowing state to exclude specified transactions, such as mutual-to-stock conversions of regulated institutions, from chapter 9 in favor of specialized statutes).

[#MBCA903]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.03 (required approvals).

[#MBCA903]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.03 (optional provision requiring domestications and conversions to obtain same regulatory approvals as would be required for equivalent mergers).

[#MBCA904]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.04 (relationship to other change-of-control laws).

[#MBCA904]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.04 (optional provision preventing domestication or conversion from varying state change-of-control or control-share statutes unless plan receives approval sufficient to directly vary those statutes).


[#MBCA920]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.20 (domestication authorized).

[#MBCA920]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.20 (foreign corporation may become domestic if organic law permits; domestic corporation may become foreign if target law permits; plan must specify required terms and may use section 1.20(k) extrinsic facts; protected-agreement merger provisions extended to domestications).

[#MBCA921]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21 (action on a plan of domestication).

[#MBCA921a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21(a) (board must adopt plan of domestication).

[#MBCA921b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21(b) (board must recommend plan to shareholders unless conflicts or section 8.26 justify withholding recommendation; basis for not recommending must be disclosed).

[#MBCA921c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21(c) (board may condition shareholder approval or plan effectiveness on specified terms).

[#MBCA921d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21(d) (meeting notice must state domestication purpose, include or summarize plan, and attach or summarize post-domestication articles and bylaws).

[#MBCA921e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21(e) (default approval requires majority of votes entitled to be cast plus separate majority by each class or series voting group).

[#MBCA921f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21(f) (articles may limit or eliminate separate voting-group approval except where foreign articles include changes requiring section 10.04 separate vote if done as domestic amendment).

[#MBCA921g]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.21(g) (shareholders newly incurring or materially changing interest holder liability must sign separate written consent unless terms substantially identical or reduce liability).

[#MBCA922]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.22 (articles of domestication).

[#MBCA922]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.22 (domesticating corporation files signed articles stating domesticating and domesticated entities and confirming approval; must attach articles of incorporation if domesticated corporation is domestic; effective date governed by section 1.23 with special rules for foreign domesticated corporations).

[#MBCA923]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.23 (amendment and abandonment of domestication).

[#MBCA923]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.23 (plan may be amended as originally approved or as plan provides; material adverse changes require renewed shareholder approval; board may abandon before effectiveness without shareholder action, including by filing articles of abandonment).

[#MBCA924]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.24 (effect of domestication).

[#MBCA924]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.24 (domesticated corporation is same entity as domesticating corporation; all property, rights, liabilities, and proceedings continue without transfer or impairment; preserves appraisal enforcement against foreign domesticated corporation via secretary-of-state agency; interest holder liability preserved or cut off using before-after effectiveness rules; protects charitable assets from diversion).


[#MBCA930]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.30 (conversion authorized).

[#MBCA930]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.30 (domestic corporation may become domestic or foreign eligible entity if organic law permits; domestic and foreign eligible entities may become domestic corporation; supplies approval mechanics when eligible entity's organic law silent; protected-agreement merger provisions extended to conversions).

[#MBCA931]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.31 (plan of conversion).

[#MBCA931]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.31 (written plan must specify converting entity, converted entity's jurisdiction and type, manner and basis for converting shares to new interests, full text of written organic rules for converted entity, and any other lawful provisions; may use section 1.20(k) extrinsic facts).

[#MBCA932]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.32 (action on a plan of conversion).

[#MBCA932a]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.32(a) (board must adopt plan of conversion).

[#MBCA932b]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.32(b) (board must recommend plan unless conflicts or section 8.26 justify withholding recommendation; basis must be disclosed).

[#MBCA932c]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.32(c) (board may condition approval or effectiveness).

[#MBCA932d]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.32(d) (meeting notice must state plan consideration purpose, include or summarize plan, and attach or summarize converted entity's organic rules as effective after conversion).

[#MBCA932e]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.32(e) (default approval requires majority of votes entitled to be cast plus separate majority by each class or series voting group).

[#MBCA932f]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.32(f) (shareholders who would become subject to interest holder liability must provide separate written consent).

[#MBCA933]: Model Bus. Corp. Act § 9.33 (articles of conversion).

[#MBCA933]: Model Bus. Corp.
